PREFACE 
    This Code constitutes a recodification of the general and permanent ordinances of the Village of Lewiston, New York. 
    Source materials used in the preparation of the Code were the 1978 Code, as supplemented through Local Law No. 2-2009, adopted October 5, 2009, and legislation subsequently adopted by the village. The source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof. The absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the Code. By use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this Code, the reader can locate any section of the 1978 Code, as supplemented, and any legislation included herein. 
    The chapters of the Code have been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order, and the various sections within each chapter have been catchlined to facilitate usage. Notes which tie related sections of the Code together and which refer to relevant state law have been included. A table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the Code is included at the back of this Code. 
Chapter and Section Numbering System 
    The chapter and section numbering system used in this Code is the same system used in many state and local government codes. Each section number consists of two parts separated by a dash. The figure before the dash refers to the chapter number, and the figure after the dash refers to the position of the section within the chapter. Thus, the second section of chapter 1 is numbered 1-2, and the first section of chapter 6 is 6-1. Under this system, each section is identified with its chapter, and at the same time new sections can be inserted in their proper place by using the decimal system for amendments. For example, if new material consisting of one section that would logically come between sections 6-1 and 6-2 is desired to be added, such new section would be numbered 6-1.5. New articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or, in the case of articles, may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject, and, in the case of divisions, may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject. The next successive number shall be assigned to the new article or division. Care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters. 
Page Numbering System 
    The page numbering system used in this Code is a prefix system. The letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume. The number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion. In the case of a chapter of the Code, the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter. In the case of an appendix to the Code, the letter immediately to the left of the colon indicates the letter of the appendix. The following are typical parts of codes of ordinances, which may or may not appear in this Code at this time, and their corresponding prefixes: 
CODE CD1:1 CODE APPENDIX CDA:1 CODE COMPARATIVE TABLES CCT:1 STATE LAW REFERENCE TABLE SLT:1 CODE INDEX CDi:1  
Index 
    The index has been prepared with the greatest of care. Each particular item has been placed under several headings, some of which are couched in lay phraseology, others in legal terminology, and still others in language generally used by local government officials and employees. There are numerous cross references within the index itself that stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which the user is interested. 
Looseleaf Supplements 
    A special feature of this publication is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing of the publication. With this system, the publication will be kept up to date. Subsequent amendatory legislation will be properly edited, and the affected page or pages will be reprinted. These new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the publication, with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages. 
    Keeping this publication up to date at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the publication. As revised pages are received, it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions. It is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and, in addition, that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes. 
Acknowledgments 
    This publication was under the direct supervision of Roger D. Merriam, Senior Code Attorney, and Ellen Torof, Editor, of the Municipal Code Corporation, Tallahassee, Florida. Credit is gratefully given to the other members of the publisher's staff for their sincere interest and able assistance throughout the project. 
    The publisher is most grateful to Ms. Anne Welch, Village Clerk-Treasurer, for cooperation and assistance during the progress of the work on this publication. It is hoped that her efforts and those of the publisher have resulted in a Code of Ordinances which will make the active law of the village readily accessible to all citizens and which will be a valuable tool in the day-to-day administration of the village's affairs.

Chapter 1 - GENERAL PROVISIONS 

Sec. 1-1. - How Code designated and cited. 
    The ordinances and local laws embraced in this and the following chapters and sections shall constitute and be designated the "Village Code of the Village of Lewiston, New York," and may be so cited. Such Code may also be cited as the "Lewiston Village Code." 
(Code 1978, § 1-1) 
State Law reference- Codification of local laws, Municipal Home Rule Law § 20(3.). 
Sec. 1-2. - Catchlines of sections. 
    The catchlines of the several sections of this Code printed in boldface type are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the section and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections, nor as any part of the section, nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted. 
(Code 1978, § 1-2) 
Sec. 1-3. - Definitions and rules of construction. 
    In the construction of this Code, and of all ordinances and local laws, the following rules shall be observed, unless such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the village board of trustees: 
    Code. The term "the Code" or "this Code" means the Village Code of the Village of Lewiston, New York, as designated in section 1-1. 
    Computation of time. Whenever a notice is required to be given or an act to be done, a certain length of time before any proceeding shall be had, the day on which such notice is given, or such act is done, shall be counted in computing the time, but the day on which such proceeding is to be had shall not be counted. 
    Corporate limits, corporation limits or village limits. Whenever the term "corporate limits," "corporation limits" or "village limits" is used, such term means the legal boundary of the Village of Lewiston. 
    County. The term "the county" or "this county" means the County of Niagara in the State of New York. 
    Delegation of authority. Whenever a provision appears requiring the head of a department of the village to do some act or make certain inspections, it is to be construed to authorize the head of the department to designate, delegate and authorize subordinates to perform the required act or make the required inspection unless the terms of the provision or section designate otherwise. 
    Gender. A word importing only one gender shall extend and be applied to the other and to any other person as herein defined. 
    Interpretation. In the interpretation and application of any provision of this Code, it shall be held to be the minimum requirements adopted for the promotion of the public health, safety, comfort, convenience and general welfare. Where any provision of the Code imposes greater restrictions upon the subject matter than other more general provisions imposed by the Code, the provision imposing the greater restriction or regulation shall be deemed to be controlling. 
    Joint authority. All words giving a joint authority to three or more persons or officers shall be construed as giving such authority to a majority of such persons or officers. 
    Keeper, proprietor. The terms "keeper" and "proprietor" mean and include persons, firms, associations, corporations, clubs and partnerships, whether acting by themselves or through a servant, agent or employee. 
    May, shall. The term "may" is permissive, and the term "shall" is mandatory. 
    Mayor. Whenever the term "mayor" is used, it means the mayor of the Village of Lewiston; and where a provision of this Code, an ordinance or a local law shall direct that an act be performed or decision be made by the mayor, such expression shall be deemed to include not only the mayor but the acting or deputy mayor in the absence of the mayor, or any member of the board of trustees designated by the board or the mayor to perform the act or exercise the discretion referred to; or except as otherwise provided by law. 
    Month. The term "month" means a calendar month. 
    Name of officer. Whenever the name of an officer is given, it shall be construed as though the terms "of the Village of Lewiston" were added. 
    Nontechnical and technical words. Words and phrases shall be construed according to the common and approved usage of the language; but technical words and phrases and such others as may have acquired a peculiar and appropriate meaning in law shall be construed and understood according to such meaning. 
    Number. A word importing the singular number only may extend and be applied to several persons and things as well as to one person and thing, and vice versa. 
    Oath. The term "oath" shall be construed to include an affirmation in all cases in which, by law, an affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in such cases, the terms "swear" and "sworn" shall be equivalent to the terms "affirm" and "affirmed." 
    Or, and. The term "or" may be read "and," and the term "and" may be read "or," if the sense requires it. 
    Owner. The term "owner," applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint owner, tenant in common, tenant in partnership, joint tenant, or tenant by the entirety, of the whole or of a part of such building or land. 
    Person. The term "person" shall be any individual, firm, partnership, association, corporation or organization of any kind. 
    Personal property. The term "personal property" includes every species of property except real property, as herein described. 
    Preceding, following. The terms "preceding" and "following" mean next before and next after, respectively. 
    Premises. Whenever the term "premises" is used, it means place or places. 
    Property. The term "property" includes real and personal property. 
    Real property. The term "real property" includes lands, tenements and hereditaments. 
    Seal. Whenever the term "seal" is used, it means the village or corporate seal. 
    Sidewalk. The term "sidewalk" means any portion of a street between the curbline and the adjacent property line, intended for the use of pedestrians. 
    Signature or subscription. The "signature" or "subscription" of a person includes a mark when the person cannot write. 
    State. The term "the state" or "this state" shall be construed to mean the State of New York. 
    State law. All references to state law shall be construed as references to the official version of the New York State Consolidated Laws, as may be amended from time to time. 
    Street. The term "street" includes, but shall not be limited to, streets, avenues, boulevards, roads, alleys, lanes, designated rights-of-way laid out for future development, viaducts and all other public highways in the village. 
    Tenant, occupant. The term "tenant" or "occupant," applied to a building or land, includes any person holding a written or oral lease or who occupies the whole or a part of such building or land, either alone or with others. 
    Tense. Words used in the past or present tense include the future as well as the past and present. 
    The village, this village, the corporation or this corporation. Whenever the term "the village," "this village," "the corporation" or "this corporation" is used, it shall be construed as if the terms "of Lewiston, New York" followed them. 
    Trustee. The term "trustee" means any person elected or appointed to that office. 
    Village board of trustees or board of trustees. Whenever the term "village board of trustees" or "board of trustees" is used, it shall be construed to mean the Board of Trustees of the Village of Lewiston. 
    Village employee. The term "village employee" means a nonunion village employee of the Village of Lewiston, New York. 
    Week. The term "week" shall be construed to mean seven days. 
    Written, in writing. The term "written" or "in writing" shall be construed to include any representation of words, letters or figures, whether by printing or otherwise. 
(Code 1978, § 1-3) 
State Law reference- Similar definitions, General Construction Law § 10 et seq. 
Sec. 1-4. - Amendments or additions to Code. 
(a)  All local laws passed subsequent to this Code which amend, repeal or in any way affect this Code, may be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this Code and printed for inclusion therein, or in the case of repealed chapters, sections and subsections or any part thereof, by subsequent local laws, such repealed portions may be excluded from the Code by omission from reprinted pages affected thereby and the subsequent local laws as numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie evidence of such subsequent local laws until such time that this Code and subsequent local laws numbered or omitted are readopted as a new code by the village board of trustees. 
(b)  Amendments to any of the provisions of this Code should be made by amending such provisions by specific reference to the section of this Code in substantially the following language: "That section (or article or chapter) _______ of the Village Code of the Village of Lewiston, New York, is hereby amended to read as follows:... ." The new provisions may then be set out in full as desired. 
(c)  In the event a new section not heretofore existing in the Code is to be added, the following language may be used: 
"That the Village Code of the Village of Lewiston, New York, is hereby amended by adding a section (or article or chapter) to be numbered as follows _______, which said section shall read as follows:... ." The new section may then be set out in full as desired. 
(d)  When the village board of trustees desires to enact a local law of a general and permanent nature on a subject not heretofore existing in the Code, which said board desires to incorporate into the Code, a section in substantially the following language may be made a part of the local law: "Section _______. It is the intention of the governing body, and it is hereby ordained, that the provisions of this local law shall become and be made a part of the Village Code of the Village of Lewiston, New York, and the sections of this local law may be renumbered to accomplish such intention." 
(e)  All sections, articles, chapters or provisions of this Code desired to be repealed should be specifically repealed by section number, article number or chapter number, as the case may be. 
(Code 1978, § 1-4) 
Sec. 1-5. - Effect of repeal of ordinances or local laws. 
(a)  The repeal of an ordinance or local law shall not revive any ordinances or local laws in force before or at the time the ordinances or local laws repealed took effect. 
(b)  The repeal of an ordinance or local law shall not affect any punishment or penalty incurred before the repeal took effect, nor any suit, prosecution or proceeding pending at the time of the repeal, for an offense committed or cause of action arising under the ordinance or local law repealed. 
(Code 1978, § 1-5) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, General Construction Law § 90 et seq. 
Sec. 1-6. - Altering Code. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to change or amend by additions or deletions any part or portion of this Code, or to insert or delete pages, or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with such Code in any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the village to be misrepresented thereby. Any person violating this section shall be punished as provided in section 1-7. 
(Code 1978, § 1-6) 
State Law reference- Tampering with public records, Penal Law §§ 175.20, 175.25. 
Sec. 1-7. - General penalty; continuing violations. 
(a)  Whenever in this Code or in any ordinance, resolution or local law of the village any act is prohibited or is made or declared to be unlawful or an offense, or whenever in such Code, ordinance, resolution or local law the doing of any act is required or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful, where no specific fine or penalty is provided therefor, the violation of any provisions of this Code or any such ordinance, resolution or local law shall constitute an offense and shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $250.00. Each day any violation of any provision of this Code or of any such ordinance, resolution or local law shall continue shall constitute a separate offense. 
(b)  In addition to the fine hereinabove provided, any condition caused or permitted to exist in violation of any of the provisions of this Code or any such ordinance, resolution or local law shall be deemed a public nuisance and may be by the village abated as provided by law, and each day that such condition continues shall be regarded as a new and separate offense. 
(Code 1978, § 1-7) 
State Law reference- Penalties for violation of village legislation, Penal Law §§ 55.10, 70.15, 80.05, 80.10, Village Law § 20-2006, Municipal Home Rule Law § 10(4.)(b.). 
Sec. 1-8. - Prosecution where different penalties exist for same offense. 
    In all cases where the same offense may be made punishable, or shall be created by different clauses or sections of this Code, ordinances, resolutions or local laws of the village, the prosecuting officer may elect under which to proceed; but not more than one recovery shall be had against the same person for the same offense. 
(Code 1978, § 1-8) 
Sec. 1-9. - Penalties not exclusive. 
    Obedience to the provisions hereinafter set forth may be enforced by criminal information for the penalties herein prescribed as well as by prosecution of the offender as provided in section 1-7, or by civil action for a penalty, or by civil remedy at law or equity by way of injunction, or otherwise to abate or prevent a violation of the provisions of this Code. Neither a judgment in, nor the pendency of a criminal prosecution for an alleged violation of the provisions of this Code, nor a judgment in or the pendency of a civil action at law or in equity shall be a bar to the other form of proceeding. The imposition of a penalty for a violation of this Code shall not excuse the violation or permit it to continue, and the remedies herein provided for penalties and civil action to enjoin or abate a violation shall be cumulative. 
(Code 1978, § 1-9) 
Sec. 1-10. - Severability of parts of Code. 
    The sections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses and phrases of this Code are severable, and if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph or section of this Code shall be declared unconstitutional by the valid judgment or decree of a court of competent jurisdiction, such unconstitutionality shall not affect any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs and sections of this Code. 
(Code 1978, § 1-10) 
Chapter 2 - ADMINISTRATION 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 2-1. - Flag. 
    The village hereby adopts the flag as presented to the village board of trustees by historian Dr. S. N. Bruni and so designed by him. 
(Code 1978, § 2-1; Res. of 5-7-1973) 
Sec. 2-2. - Seal. 
    The village hereby adopts the design of the flag presented to the village by S. N. Bruni on May 7, 1973, as the official village seal. 
(Code 1978, § 2-2; Res. of 5-7-1973) 
State Law reference- Seal authorized, Village Law § 1-102. 
Sec. 2-3. - Terms of boards and commissions; attendance. 
(a)  The terms of office of all members appointed to commissions and boards created by the board of trustees whether by local law or resolution shall commence on the day of the first organizational meeting in the year of appointment and shall expire on the day before the first organizational meeting in the year of expiration of the term appointed to. 
(b)  The requirements of the Village Law of the state, as the same provides for the terms of office and numbers of members of the boards and commissions, are hereby superseded within the village for all matters and things which may properly be the subject of control by a local law herein adopted by the board of trustees of the village. 
(c)  Upon failure to personally attend three consecutive regular meetings, a member of any village board or commission heretofore appointed to such board or commission shall be deemed to have resigned therefrom. The chairman of such board or commission may excuse an absence after receiving a request from such member. The mayor may excuse an absence after receiving a request from a chairman of a board or commission. Any member whose absence is validly excused by a chairman of a board or commission, or mayor as the case may be, shall be deemed to be in attendance at the meeting for the sole purpose of determining whether a member has had three consecutive absences. 
(Code 1978, § 2-3; L.L. No. 6-1975, §§ 1, 2; L.L. No. 6-1980, § 1) 
Sec. 2-4. - Enclosure of information of public interest in village bills authorized. 
(a)  Enclosures may be included with the village tax bills or water bills. 
(b)  Such enclosures shall consist only of public information which is of interest to the local residents. 
(c)  Such enclosures, bulletins, circulars or brochures shall be of a nonpartisan nature and shall reflect no one political philosophy or the furtherance thereof. 
(Code 1978, § 2-5; L.L. No. 7-1968) 
Sec. 2-5. - Conduct of village business, affairs. 
    The conduct of business and affairs of the village shall be through departments, boards, commissions and/or committees established and organized for the purpose by resolution of the village board of trustees. Each such department shall be under the supervision of a member of the village board of trustees appointed for that purpose. 
(Code 1978, § 2-6) 
Sec. 2-6. - Removal of papers from village offices. 
    No person shall carry out or remove any papers, plans, specifications, documents or records of any property whatsoever belonging to the village, from any of the village offices or rooms, in the respective departments where such papers, specifications, plans, documents or records properly belong, except under the direction of the mayor or village board of trustees, or pursuant to court subpoena served upon the village clerk-treasurer. 
(Code 1978, § 2-7) 
Sec. 2-7. - Failure to pay fees or charges due village. 
    Any fees or charges under this Code which are due the village and not paid will be added to the tax roll. 
(Code 1978, § 2-8) 
Sec. 2-8. - Memorial Day observance. 
(a)  The board of trustees may appropriate in any year an amount as hereinafter provided for the purpose of defraying the expense of the proper observance of Memorial or Declaration Day which amount shall be assessed, levied and collected in the same manner as other village expenses. 
(b)  The amount which may be so appropriated in any year shall not exceed the sum of $750.00. 
(c)  Such monies shall be expended by the board of trustees, except that the board of trustees may designate the American Legion, Veterans of Foreign Wars, AMVETS, American Veterans of World War II, or similar organizations, or more than one of such organizations to have charge of such observance and may pay the expense of such within the limits herein provided to the organization designated upon the voucher of one or more of the officers of such organization when duly approved by it. 
(d)  A designation of an organization shall be made by resolution of the board of trustees and shall be on such conditions as the board of trustees determines to be in the best interests of the village. 
(Code 1978, § 2-9; L.L. No. 5-1978, § 1) 
Sec. 2-9. - Procedure for enacting zoning amendments. 
    Every amendment to appendix B to the village Code constituting the zoning law of the village enacted by the village board shall be posted conspicuously at or near the main entrance to the office of the village clerk-treasurer for a period of ten days after its enactment. There shall be no requirement to publish the amendment or any map incorporated or referred to therein in any official newspaper. Reference to the enactment of the local law which makes the amendment shall be reflected in the minutes of the village board. The local law will take effect with the filing of same in accordance with Municipal Home Rule Law and upon posting. Such local law shall take effect, in any event from the date of its service as against a person served personally with a true copy of same. The section supersedes Village Law § 7-706(2.). 
(Code 1978, § 2-10; L.L. No. 3-1989, § 2) 
State Law reference- Authority to supersede provisions in Village Law, Municipal Home Rule Law § 10(1.(ii)e.(3)). 
Secs. 2-10-2-38. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BOARD OF TRUSTEES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Village boards generally, Village Law § 4-412. 

Sec. 2-39. - Election; terms. 
    Elections for two members of the board of trustees shall be held biennially on the third Tuesday in June of even-numbered years. Members shall hold office for four years. 
(Code 1978, § 2-19; Res. of 9-16-1974, §§ 1, 2) 
Sec. 2-40. - Meeting times. 
    Regular meetings of the board shall be at 6:30 p.m., local time, on the first and third Mondays of each month, except that there shall be no first Monday meetings during June, July and August of each year. 
(Code 1978, § 2-20; Mo. of 4-17-1961; Res. of 4-7-1975) 
Sec. 2-41. - Meetings to be public; exception. 
    All meetings of the village board of trustees shall be open to the public; provided, however, that the board shall have the authority to sit in executive session, which session shall be closed to the public. 
(Code 1978, § 2-21) 
Sec. 2-42. - Rules for conduct of meetings. 
    The village board of trustees shall determine and prescribe the rules for the conduct of its meetings and the order of business thereat. 
(Code 1978, § 2-22) 
State Law reference- Authority to prescribe rules, Village Law § 4-412(2.). 
Sec. 2-43. - Minutes of meetings. 
    The village clerk-treasurer shall keep a journal of the proceedings of the village board of trustees, which journal shall be open to public inspection in the office of the village clerk-treasurer. 
Sec. 2-44. - Standing committees of village board. 
    At its first meeting in each official year, the village board of trustees by resolution shall establish the standing committees of the board, and shall prescribe the functions and duties thereof. 
(Code 1978, § 2-21) 
State Law reference- Official year, Village Law § 3-302(1.). 
Sec. 2-45. - Appointment of chairman of standing committees. 
    At the meeting of the village board of trustees described in section 2-44, the mayor shall appoint one trustee as chairman of each standing committee established by the board. 
(Code 1978, § 2-25) 
Sec. 2-46. - Compensation. 
    The annual salary of each trustee of the village shall be as may be set from time to time by the village board of trustees per adoption of budget in accordance with the procedure set forth in the village law, per April 16, 1984, and kept on file in the office of the village clerk-treasurer. 
(Code 1978, § 2-26; L.L. No. 3-1975, § 1; L.L. No. 9-1975, § 1; L.L. No. 6-1977, § 1; L.L. No. 12-1980, § 1; Res. of 5-7-1984) 
Secs. 2-47-2-66. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-67. - Salary establishment procedure for elected officials. 
    The board of trustees of the village shall fix the salaries of all elected officers through the inclusion of said salaries in the schedule of wages set forth in the budget and upon the adoption of said budget in accordance with the procedure set forth in the Village Law, said salary shall be thereby fixed. 
(Code 1978, § 2-37; L.L. No. 8-1980, § 1) 
Sec. 2-68. - Treasurer's term; position of deputy treasurer created. 
    The term of office of the village treasurer shall be four years. 
(1)  The position of deputy treasurer in the village is hereby created, and the term of office of the deputy treasurer shall be one year. 
(2)  The deputy treasurer is authorized to act in the absence of the clerk-treasurer. 
(Code 1978, § 2-38; Res. of 9-16-1974, § 5; Res. of 11-1-1999; L.L. No. 2-1999) 
State Law reference- Terms of office, Village Law § 3-302; treasurer, Village Law § 4-408. 
Sec. 2-69. - Clerk's term; position of deputy clerk created. 
    The term of office of the village clerk shall be four years. 
(1)  The position of deputy clerk in the village is hereby created, and the term of office of the deputy clerk shall be one year. 
(2)  The deputy clerk is authorized to act in the absence of the clerk-treasurer. 
(Code 1978, § 2-39; Res. of 9-16-1974, § 5; Res. of 11-1-1999; L.L. No. 2-1999) 
State Law reference- Terms of office, Village Law § 3-302; clerk, Village Law § 4-402. 
Sec. 2-70. - Expense money restrictions. 
(a)  The clerk-treasurer is authorized to advance such sums as are reasonably necessary to all employees, officers or officials to finance official travel expenses by such person. The amount of any such advance shall not exceed $200.00 unless specifically authorized by the village board of trustees. 
(b)  A person seeking such an advance shall apply to the clerk-treasurer for such advance on such forms as may be required by him, and shall account to the clerk-treasurer for the expenses of such travel and repay any unexpended funds to the village within five days after returning from such travel. The clerk-treasurer is hereby authorized to make payment of any such advance. 
(c)  The village may withhold from the salary of any official, officer or employee the amount of any unreturned advance where the advance exceeds actual reimbursable expenses and such official, officer or employee fails to return the excess within a period of time to be specified by the board. 
(Code 1978, § 2-40; Res. of 4-1-1969) 
Sec. 2-71. - Refusing to obey or resisting officers in discharge of duty prohibited. 
    No person shall refuse to obey or shall resist any officer or employee of the village in the discharge of his duty. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, § 15; Code 1978, § 2-41) 
State Law reference- Obstructing government administration, Penal Law § 195.05. 
Sec. 2-72. - Pension benefits. 
    The village hereby elects to come under the provisions of Retirement and Social Security Law § 75-b, in relation to establishing noncontributory retirement plans and ordinary death benefits for state employees and members of participating employees"; the members' contributions in the employ of the village shall be suspended and the effective date of such suspension shall be the payroll period beginning on May 24, 1970. 
(Code 1978, § 2-42; Res. of 5-19-1970) 
Editor's note- Subsequent to the resolution of May 19, 1970, the village has adopted various additional benefits relating to the pension and retirement plan. Such resolutions are not included herein, but may be found on file in the village offices. 
Sec. 2-73. - Guaranteed ordinary death benefits. 
    The village hereby elects to provide the benefits of Retirement and Social Security Law § 360-b, as presently or hereafter amended, to become effective with the payroll period beginning on June 3, 1973. 
(Code 1978, § 2-43; Res. of 5-30-1973) 
Sec. 2-74. - Work hours. 
    Normal work hours for village employees shall be as follows: 
(1)  Department of public works: 
a.  Eight-hour day. 
b.  One-half hour unpaid lunch. 
c.  40-hour week unless otherwise scheduled by the department head. 
(2)  Reserved. 
(3)  Administrative offices: 
a.  35-hour to 40-hour week. 
b.  One hour unpaid lunch. 
c.  Unless otherwise scheduled by department head: 
1.  Overtime will be paid after 40 hours have been worked. 
2.  Holidays, vacation days and jury days will be counted as days worked. 
(Code 1978, § 2-44; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 5-28-1981; Res. of 12-21-1981) 
Sec. 2-75. - Holidays. 
    Nonunion full-time village employees shall receive holidays subject to the following regulations: 
(1)  Scheduled holidays: New Year's Day; Martin Luther King, Jr. Day, Patriots Day; Memorial Day; Independence Day, July fourth; Labor Day; Columbus Day, Veterans Day; Thanksgiving Day and the day after; Christmas Day; Good Friday; Christmas Eve, one-half day in the afternoon; New Year's Eve, one-half day in the afternoon. 
(2)  One floating holiday, the time to be chosen by the employee, subject to approval by the department head. 
(3)  A holiday falling on a Saturday shall be celebrated on the preceding Friday. 
(4)  A holiday falling on Sunday shall be celebrated on the following Monday. 
(5)  An employee may, with the permission of the department head and board, observe a holiday one day other than the actual day of holiday; providing essential and adequate services are covered. 
(6)  Pay for time off and straight time plus holiday pay for work on a holiday with the stipulation that one must work as scheduled the day before and the day after a holiday unless excusably absent. 
(Code 1978, § 2-45; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978) 
Sec. 2-76. - Vacations. 
    Full-time village employees shall be entitled to vacations in accordance with the following regulations: 
(1)  Eligible vacation will be taken within the fiscal year June 1 through May 31. 
(2)  Vacation requests shall be submitted to the department head in writing by May 1. 
(3)  Seniority will normally be the basis for scheduling. 
(4)  An employee's vacation time will be based on the following schedule, after completion of the stipulated continuous service: 
Years of Service Vacation 1 1 week 2 2 weeks 5 3 weeks 10 3 weeks, plus 1 day with an additional day per year to a maximum of 4 weeks 15 4 weeks, plus 1 day, with an additional day per year to a maximum of 5 weeks 20 5 weeks  
(5)  After ten years of service an employee is permitted to carry over one week of his three weeks to add to another year's eligibility to make a total of four weeks vacation. This and any extended vacation schedule must be with the approval of the department head. 
(6)  Eligibility for vacations. An employee must have accumulated six months of active employment to be eligible for vacation in the following year. 
(7)  A holiday falling during vacation will result in an extra day's pay. 
(8)  In addition to regular vacation, when an employee leaves village service during the course of the year, for reasons of retirement or death, he shall receive a vacation credit of one day for each month worked during the fiscal year not to exceed ten days for an employee. 
(Code 1978, § 2-246; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 5-28-1981; Res. of 5-7-1984) 
Sec. 2-77. - Jury pay. 
    Employees of the village shall be eligible for jury pay based on the difference between their basic hourly pay for a 40-hour workweek and the jury pay for actual time spent on jury services. 
(Code 1978, § 2-47; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978) 
Sec. 2-78. - Military leave allowance. 
(a)  Permanent employees of the village shall be eligible for military leave allowance based on the following schedule: 
Years of Service Allowance 1 1 week 2 2 weeks  
(b)  The basis for payment of military leave allowance shall be as follows: the amount shall be the amount payable for a 40-hour week less the amount received as base military pay for a week multiplied by the number of weeks of allowance as determined in subsection (a) of this section. 
(Code 1978, § 2-48; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 3-21-1994) 
Sec. 2-79. - Sick leave allowance. 
    Full-time employees of the village shall be eligible for sick leave allowance in accordance with the following regulations: 
(1)  On completion of 90 days of service, three days. 
(2)  One additional day is added for each month thereafter up to a maximum of one 200 days. 
(3)  Verification: 
a.  Sick leave allowance commences with the first day of illness provided the employee is hospitalized. 
b.  Paid from first day if verified by a physician. 
c.  No pay if not verified by a physician until the fourth day and then no pay unless verified by a physician. 
(4)  No sick leave allowance will be paid if vacation, holiday or other benefits have been paid for the same day. 
(5)  Benefits such as compensation or NYS disability will be deducted from sick leave allowance. 
(6)  Sick leave may only be used for actual illness. 
(7)  Upon the recommendation of his supervisor, after all sick time and vacation time have been exhausted, a full-time employee who has been continuously employed by the village for five years will be granted by the village board of trustees one-half pay (one-half salary or 20 hours weekly) for six months. 
(8)  Two accumulated sick days may be used each year for illness of an immediate family member. Up to ten days of unused family illness days may be accumulated. Immediate family is defined under section 2-81(b). 
(9)  In addition to regular sick leave allowance when an employee leaves village service during the course of the year, for reasons of retirement or death, he shall receive one day's salary for every ten unused sick days not to exceed 200 accumulated unused sick days. 
(Code 1978, § 2-49; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 6-16-1980; Res. of 11-15-1982; Res. of 6-1-1983; Res. of 5-7-1984) 
Sec. 2-80. - Personal leave. 
    Village employees shall be eligible for three days per year of personal leave, if necessary, after one year of service, subject to approval of each employee's department head. The employee must give sufficient notice. Such leave is not cumulative, and may not be used in conjunction with other types of leave. 
(Code 1978, § 2-50; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 6-16-1980) 
Sec. 2-81. - Funeral leave. 
(a)  An employee with 30 or more days service is eligible for five days with pay for funeral arrangements for the employee's immediate family. 
(b)  The term "immediate family," for purposes of this section, means wife, husband, children, parents of the employee or spouse, brothers and sisters of the employee or spouse, step-children. 
(c)  An employee with 30 or more days service is eligible for three days with pay for funeral arrangements for the employee's extended family. 
(d)  The term "extended family," for purposes of this section, means grandparents, grandchildren, great grandparents, great grandchildren, first cousins, uncles, aunts, nieces and nephews of the employee or spouse. 
(Code 1978, § 2-51; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978) 
Sec. 2-82. - Overtime meal allowance. 
    Six dollars, or more at the supervisor's discretion, will be allowed a village employee for meals if the employee works two hours not within the employee's normal scheduled hours. The $6.00 or more must be spent on a meal, the tab to be presented to the clerk-treasurer for petty cash allowance. The money shall not be spent on alcoholic beverages. 
(Code 1978, § 2-52; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 6-16-1980; Res. of 5-7-1984; Res. of 3-19-1990) 
Sec. 2-83. - Health and life insurance benefits. 
(a)  For full-time employees, health insurance options may be established from time to time by the village board of trustees, and such options shall be on file in the office of the village clerk-treasurer. 
(b)  Part-time employees can enjoy the privilege of participation in the health insurance plans available as established by the village through full reimbursement of the premium cost to the village. No flexible spending accounts will be funded by the village for part-time employees. All employees who join the plan are, upon leaving, eligible to remain in the plan for nine months after severance provided they reimburse the village. 
(c)  Upon retirement, at age 55 years (minimum), the village will pay the following portions of the most favorable rate health insurance coverage costs: 
Years of Employment Village 
(percent) Member 
(percent) 10 25 75 15 50 50 20 75 25 25 100 0  
Flexible spending accounts will not continue to be maintained by the village for employees after their retirement. 
(Code 1978, § 2-53; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 6-16-1980; Res. of 5-7-1984; Res. of 5-20-1985; Res. of 1-23-1989; Res. of 5-31-1989; Res. of 4-15-1991; Res. of 12-18-1995; Res. of 3-22-2004) 
Sec. 2-84. - Reports regarding employee absences and vacations. 
    Each department head shall: 
(1)  Prepare a monthly report, by employee, showing absences, by type, during the month and eligible time coming by type, as of the end of each month. Such reports are to be filed with the clerk-treasurer by the end of the fifth working day of each new month. 
(2)  Prepare a master vacation schedule and file with the clerk-treasurer by July 1. Schedule changes are permitted with approval of department heads and mayor. 
(Code 1978, § 2-54; Res. of 6-1-1974; Res. of 4-17-1978) 
Sec. 2-85. - Longevity pay. 
    Long-term full-time employees of the village who have completed the requisite number of years of continuous full-time employment prior to the beginning of the fiscal year shall be eligible for longevity pay in accordance with the following schedule. Longevity pay shall annually be paid to those eligible employees on the first regular payday in December, and the amount shall be included in the regular paycheck. 
Years of service completed 
prior to start of fiscal year Annual longevity 
pay amount 10 $100.00 15  150.00 20  200.00 25  250.00 30  300.00  
(Code 1978, § 2-55; Res. of 6-16-1975; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 4-18-1988) 
Sec. 2-86. - Mileage allowance. 
    Mileage allowance for the approved use of personal vehicles shall be in accordance with the standard of the United States Internal Revenue Service. 
(Code 1978, § 2-56; Res. of 4-17-1978; Res. of 7-16-1979; Res. of 5-28-1981; Res. of 5-29-1992) 
Sec. 2-87. - Residency requirements. 
    Before an appointment to a position as an employee of the village in the competitive class, as defined by the Civil Service Law, a person shall first be a resident of the village and any person so appointed must during the employee's tenure remain a village resident, subject to the restrictions of Public Officers Law §§ 3, 30. When any such employee shall cease to be a resident of the village of said position shall thereby become vacant. The village board of trustees, at its discretion, may waive the residency requirement. 
(Code 1978, § 2-58; L.L. No. 8-1990, § 1) 
Sec. 2-88. - Sexual harassment. 
(a)  The village finds that sexual harassment in the workplace is not merely an offensive working condition; it is against the law and is a violation of Section 703 of Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, as amended, and the New York State Human Rights Law (Executive Law § 290 et seq.). 
(b)  In accordance with the equal employment opportunity commission guidelines, unwelcome sexual advances, requests for sexual favors, or other verbal or physical conduct of a sexual nature will constitute sexual harassment when: 
(1)  Submission to the conduct is either an explicit or implicit term or condition of employment; 
(2)  Submission to or rejection of the conduct is used as a basis for an employment decision affecting the person rejecting or submitting to the conduct; or 
(3)  The conduct has the purpose or affect of unreasonably interfering with an affected person's work performance or creating an intimidating, hostile, or offensive work environment. 
(c)  Any individual believing himself to have been sexually harassed shall set forth all pertinent facts in writing and submit it to his immediate supervisor and the board of trustees inasmuch as sexual harassment is considered employee misconduct and sanctions will be taken against individuals engaging in such actions. Complaints will be investigated and disciplinary action will be determined by the board of trustees. 
(d)  Nothing in this section shall be construed to enlarge upon nor limit or abridge the rights of any person under the United States or State of New York Constitutions or the statutes of the United States or the state. 
(Code 1978, § 2-59; L.L. No. 4-1998) 
Secs. 2-89-2-112. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - MAYOR[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Responsibilities of mayor, Village Law § 4-400. 

Sec. 2-113. - Election; term. 
    The mayor shall be elected on the third Tuesday in June of appropriate even-numbered years and shall hold office for four years. 
(Code 1978, § 2-63; Res. of 9-16-1974, §§ 1, 2) 
State Law reference- Terms of office, Village Law § 3-302. 
Sec. 2-114. - Compensation. 
    The mayor's annual salary shall be as may be set from time to time by the village board of trustees per adoption of the budget in accordance with the procedure set forth in the Village Law, per April 16, 1984, and kept on file in the office of the village clerk-treasurer. 
(Code 1978, § 2-64; L.L. No. 3-1975, § 1; L.L. No. 9-1975, § 1; L.L. No. 6-1977, § 1; L.L. No. 12-1980, § 2; Res. of 5-7-1984) 
Sec. 2-115. - Removal of appointees. 
    The mayor may remove for cause, after public hearing, all persons appointed by him. 
(Code 1978, § 2-65)

DIVISION 3. - CODE OF ETHICS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to adopt code of ethics, General Municipal Law § 806. 

Sec. 2-141. - Purpose. 
    It is the purpose of this division to implement the objective of assuring the highest caliber of public administration of this village through the establishment of standards of conduct, and this is enacted pursuant to authority contained in General Municipal Law art. 18. 
(Code 1978, § 2-71; L.L. No. 3-1970, § 1) 
Sec. 2-142. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Village means any board, commission, district, council or other agency, department or unit of the government of the village. 
    Village employee means any officer or employee of the village, whether paid or unpaid and whether serving in a full-time, part-time or advisory capacity. 
(Code 1978, § 2-72; L.L. No. 3-1970, § 3) 
Sec. 2-143. - Prohibited conflicts of interest. 
    No village employee shall have any interest, financial or otherwise, direct or indirect, or engage in any business or transaction or professional activity or incur any obligation of any nature, which is in substantial conflict with the proper discharge of his duties in the public interest. 
(Code 1978, § 2-73; L.L. No. 3-1970, § 4) 
Sec. 2-144. - Standards of conduct. 
(a)  Disclosure of interest. Each village employee shall, to the extent that he is cognizant thereof, disclose in writing on the form as prescribed by the village clerk-treasurer, any interest he may have in legislation or a decision pending before the village. Such disclosure statement shall be filed with the village clerk-treasurer and with the village board, agency, commission or governmental organization with whom the conflict arose and such statement shall become a public record. 
(b)  Investments. No village employee shall hold investments in any enterprise which will be in conflict with his official duties. 
(c)  Other employment. No village employee shall accept other employment which will be in conflict with his official duties. 
(d)  Termination of employment. No village employee, after termination of his services or employment with the village, shall accept employment which will be detrimental to the village or in direct conflict with his prior village relationship. 
(Code 1978, § 2-74; L.L. No. 3-1970, § 5) 
Sec. 2-145. - Distribution of copies of division to employees. 
    The mayor shall cause a copy of this division to be distributed to every village employee. Failure to distribute any such copy or failure of any village employee to receive such copy shall have no effect on the duty of compliance with this division, nor the enforcement of provisions hereof. The mayor shall further cause a copy of this division to be kept posted conspicuously in the municipal building under the jurisdiction of the village. Failure to so post this division shall have no effect on the duty of compliance herewith, nor the enforcement provisions hereof. 
(Code 1978, § 2-75; L.L. No. 3-1970, § 7) 
Sec. 2-146. - Applicability of other laws. 
    The standards, prohibited acts and procedures established in this division are in addition to any prohibited acts, conflicts of interest provisions or procedures prescribed by statute of the state and also in addition to common law rules and judicial decisions relating to the conduct of village officers to the extent the same are more severe in their application than this division. 
(Code 1978, § 2-76; L.L. No. 3-1970, § 2) 
Sec. 2-147. - Violations; penalties. 
    In addition to any penalty contained in any other provision of law, any village employee who shall knowingly and intentionally violate any of the provisions of this division may be fined, suspended or removed from office or employment in the manner provided by law. 
(Code 1978, § 2-77; L.L. No. 3-1970, § 6) 
Secs. 2-148-2-180. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - LEGAL DEFENSE AND INDEMNIFICATION[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference- Defense and indemnification of officers and employees of public entities, Public Officers Law § 18. 

Sec. 2-181. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Employee, as used in this division, unless the context otherwise requires, means any person holding a position by election, appointment or employment in the service of the village, whether or not compensated, but shall not include an independent contractor. The term "employee" shall include a former employee, his estate or judicially appointed personal representative. 
    Legal expenses includes reasonable attorney's fees and all costs and disbursements necessary to the subject action, but does not include any costs or expenses of the plaintiff, or damages awarded to the plaintiff, should said plaintiff be successful in his action. 
(Code 1978, § 2-81; L.L. No. 7-1979, § 2) 
Sec. 2-182. - Conditions of defense. 
(a)  Upon compliance by the employee with the provisions of this division, the village shall provide for the defense of the employee in any civil action or proceeding in any state or federal court arising out of any alleged act or omission which occurred or is alleged in the complaint to have occurred while the employee was acting within the scope of his public employment or duties. This duty to provide for a defense shall not arise where such civil action or proceeding is brought by or on behalf of the village. 
(b)  Subject to the conditions set forth in subsection (a) of this section, the employee shall be entitled to be represented by the counsel retained by the village, provided, however, that the employee shall be entitled to representation by private counsel of his choice in any civil, judicial proceeding whenever retained village counsel determines, based on his investigation and review of the facts and circumstances of the case, that representation by the village-retained counsel would be inappropriate, or whenever a court of competent jurisdiction upon appropriate motion or by a special proceeding determines that a conflict of interest exists and that the employee is entitled to be represented by the counsel of his choice. The village shall notify the employee, in writing, of said determination that the employee is entitled to be represented by private counsel. The village may require as a condition to payment of the fees and expenses of such representation, that appropriate groups of such employees be represented by the same counsel. Reasonable attorney's fees and litigation expenses shall be paid by the village to such private counsel from time to time during the pendency of the civil action or proceeding subject to certification by the board of trustees that the employee is entitled to representation under the terms and conditions of this division. Any dispute with respect to representation of multiple employees by a single counsel or the amount of litigation expenses or reasonableness of attorney's fees shall be resolved by the court upon motion or by way of a special proceeding. 
(c)  Where the employee delivers process and a request for defense to the village as required by this division, the village should take the necessary steps, including the retention of private counsel under the terms and conditions provided herein, on behalf of the employee to avoid entry of a default judgment pending resolution of any questions pertaining to the obligation to provide a defense. 
(Code 1978, § 2-82; L.L. No. 7-1979, § 2) 
Sec. 2-183. - Indemnification-Generally. 
(a)  The village shall indemnify and save harmless its employees in the amount of any judgment obtained against such employee in any state or federal court, or in the amount of any settlement of the claim, provided that the act or omission from which such judgment or settlement arose, occurred while the employee was acting within the scope of his public employment or duties. The duty to indemnify and save harmless prescribed by this division shall not arise where the injury or damage resulted from intentional wrong doings or recklessness on the part of the employee. 
(b)  An employee represented by private counsel shall cause to be submitted to the board of trustees any proposed settlement which may be subject to indemnification by the village; and, if not inconsistent with the provisions of this division, the board of trustees shall review such proposed settlement as to form and amount, and shall give its approval if, in its judgment the settlement is in the best interest of the village. Nothing in this division shall be construed to authorize the village to indemnify or save harmless an employee with respect to a settlement not so reviewed and approved by the board of trustees. 
(c)  Nothing in this division shall authorize the village to indemnify or save harmless an employee with respect to punitive or exemplary damages, fines or penalties, or money recovered from an employee pursuant to State Finance Law art. 7. 
(d)  Upon entry of a final judgment against the employee, or upon the settlement of the claim, the employee shall cause to be served a copy of such judgment or settlement, personally or by certified or registered mail, within ten days of the date of entry or settlement, upon the mayor and village clerk-treasurer; and, if not inconsistent with the provisions of this division, the judgment or settlement shall be paid. 
(Code 1978, § 2-83; L.L. No. 7-1979, § 2) 
Sec. 2-184. - Same-Conditions; subject to review. 
(a)  The duty to defend or indemnify and save harmless prescribed by this division shall be conditioned upon: 
(1)  Delivery to the village clerk-treasurer by the employee of the original or a copy of any summons, complaint, process, notice, demand or pleading within five days after he is served with such document; and 
(2)  The full cooperation of the employee in the defense of such action or proceeding and in the defense of any action or proceeding against the village, based upon the same act or omission, and in the prosecution of any appeal. 
Such delivery shall be deemed a request by the employee that the village provide for his defense pursuant to this division. 
(b)  A determination by the board of trustees that the employee is not entitled to a defense under the provisions of this division shall be reviewable in a court of law. 
(Code 1978, § 2-84; L.L. No. 2-1979, § 2) 
Sec. 2-185. - Construction of division. 
(a)  The benefits of this division shall enure only to the employees as defined in section 2-181 and shall not enlarge or diminish the rights of any other party nor shall any provision of this division be construed to affect, alter or repeal any provisions of the Worker's Compensation Law. 
(b)  This division shall not in any way affect the obligation of any claimant to give notice to the village under General Municipal Law § 50 or any other provisions of law. 
(c)  The provisions of this division shall not be construed to impair, alter, limit or modify the rights and obligations of any insurer under any policy of insurance. 
(d)  The provisions of this division shall apply to all actions and proceedings pending upon the effective date thereof or thereafter instituted. 
(e)  Except as otherwise specifically provided in this division, the provisions of this division shall not be construed in any way to impair, alter, limit, modify, abrogate or restrict any immunity available to or conferred upon any department officer or employee of the village or any right to defense and/or indemnification provided for any municipal officer or employee by, in accordance with or by reason of, any other provisions of state or federal statutory or common law. 
(Code 1978, § 2-85; L.L. No. 2-1979, § 2) 
Secs. 2-186-2-208. - Reserved.

Chapter 3 - AMUSEMENTS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL

ARTICLE II. - BINGO[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Local option for conduct of bingo by certain organizations, General Municipal Law § 475 et seq.; Bingo Control Law, Executive Law § 430 et seq. 

Sec. 3-19. - License required. 
    No person other than a licensee under the provisions of General Municipal Law art. 14-H (General Municipal Law § 475 et seq.), shall conduct a game of bingo or shall lease or otherwise make available for conducting a bingo hall or other premises for any consideration whatsoever, direct or indirect. 
(Code 1978, § 4-16; Ord. of 3-17-1958, §§ 300.00, 300.10; Res. of 4-15-1963) 
Sec. 3-20. - Application for license; investigation; issuance; revocation. 
    Licenses required under this article shall be applied for, the applicants investigated, hearings held and licenses issued, suspended or revoked, pursuant to the provisions of General Municipal Law art. 14-H (General Municipal Law § 475 et seq.). 
(Code 1978, § 4-17; Ord. of 3-17-1958, § 300.30) 
Sec. 3-21. - Restrictions on conduct of games. 
    Bingo games conducted under this article shall be subject to the following restrictions: 
(1)  Prohibited lease arrangements. No bingo games shall be held, operated or conducted on or within any leased premises if rental under such lease is to be paid wholly or partly on the basis of a percentage of the receipts or net profits derived from the operation of such game. 
(2)  Use of proceeds. The entire net proceeds of any game of bingo and of any rental shall be exclusively devoted to the lawful purposes of the organization permitted to conduct the same. 
(3)  Prize limit for single games. No prize shall exceed the sum or value of $1,000.00 in any single game of bingo. 
(4)  Prize limit for series. No series of prizes on any one bingo occasion shall aggregate more than $3,000.00. 
(5)  Permitted management personnel. No person except a bona fide member of any such organization shall participate in the management or operation of such game. 
(6)  Authorized suppliers. No authorized organization licensed under the provisions of General Municipal Law art. 14-H shall purchase, lease or receive any supplies or equipment specifically designed or adapted for use in the conduct of bingo games from other than a supplier licensed under the Bingo Control Law Executive Law art. 19-B or from another authorized organization. 
(7)  Compensation for management prohibited. No person shall receive any remuneration for participating in the management or operation of any game of bingo. 
(8)  Violations. The unauthorized conduct of a bingo game and any willful violation of any provision of this article shall constitute and be punishable as a misdemeanor. 
(9)  Suppliers. No person licensed to sell bingo supplies or equipment, or their agents, shall conduct, participate in, or assist in the conduct of bingo. Nothing herein shall prohibit a licensed distributor from selling, offering for sale, or explaining a product to an authorized organization, or installing, or servicing bingo equipment, upon the premises of a bingo game licensee. 
(10)  Limited period bingo. Limited period bingo shall be conducted in accordance with the provisions of General Municipal Law art. 14-H and the rules and regulations of the state racing and wagering board. 
(11)  Statutory restrictions. Any and all other restrictions shall be as established by General Municipal Law art. 14-G or any amendments thereto establishing further restrictions. 
(Code 1978, § 4-18; Ord. of 3-17-1958, § 300.20; Res. of 4-15-1963) 
Sec. 3-22. - Applicability of state laws. 
    This article shall be subject to the provisions of General Municipal Law art. 14-H (General Municipal Law § 475 et seq.) or any amendments thereto; and further subject to the provisions of the Bingo Control Law (Executive Law § 430 et seq.) or any amendments thereto. 
(Code 1978, § 4-19; Ord. of 3-17-1958, § 300.40) 
Secs. 3-23-3-47. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - GAMES AND AMUSEMENT DEVICES 

Sec. 3-48. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Games and amusements devices means any electric, mechanical, computerized, electronic or other device, machine or implement which is either designed and intended, or used, operated or maintained, as a game, amusement or means of entertainment, including, but not limited to, the following: pinball machines, shooting galleries, computerized games, electronic games, skillboards, billiard or pool tables, electronic bowling or shuffleboard tables, table top bowling alleys and casino-type games. 
(Code 1978, § 4-20; L.L. No. 4-1981, § 2) 
Sec. 3-49. - Licenses and permits; conditions of licensing. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to own, lease, store, possess, use, operate or maintain any game or amusement device for commercial or business purposes, in or upon any premises within the village except in conformity with the provisions of this article and only after having previously obtained all licenses and permits as required herein. 
(b)  A separate premises permit shall be required for each building, facility, structure or other premises in which games or amusement devices are owned, leased, stored, possessed, used, operated or maintained. 
(c)  Applications for permits and licenses shall be made in writing on forms provided by the village clerk-treasurer, and shall be filed in the office of the village clerk-treasurer during regular business hours. Every such application shall provide for such information as the board of trustees may, from time to time, direct or require by rule, resolution or order. No application shall be accepted for filing unless fully completed, signed and notarized, and unless accompanied by payment of all application fees provided for elsewhere in this section. 
(d)  No license or permit may be granted or issued pursuant to this section unless and until all of the provisions of this article are fully complied with. In addition to the foregoing requirement, the board of trustees, as licensing body, shall consider the following factors before passing upon any application hereunder: the possible effects on the public health, peace, safety, comfort and welfare, including, but not limited to, the size, floor area, design and location of the premises; the nature and type of game or amusement device proposed to be used; the proposed hours and days of operation; the proximity of residential uses; the impact on municipal services, facilities and public areas; compatibility with surrounding business uses; potential increase in pedestrian and vehicular traffic; the adequacy of existing and proposed fire safety devices, such as sprinklers, alarms, extinguishers and fire exits; the potential for increased noise and other noxious disturbances; and compliance with all fire, building, zoning, plumbing and other ordinances and laws. 
(e)  Issuance; renewal. 
(1)  In the event that the board of trustees shall deem it advisable to grant the application for a permit or license, the village clerk-treasurer, after payment of the annual fees for licenses and permits provided for elsewhere in this section, shall issue the appropriate license and/or permit. Licenses and permits shall be issued on an annual basis only, and shall expire on December 31 next succeeding the date of issuance thereof, and no such license or permit shall be transferable. 
(2)  In the event that a license or permit issued hereunder shall not be renewed, and the annual renewal fee paid therefor, on or before January 15 next succeeding the date of expiration of such license or permit, then the same shall be null and void and of no further force or effect, and the holder thereof shall be required to file a new application, and pay a new application fee, before any such license or permit may be validly reinstated by the board of trustees and lawfully reissued and renewed by the village clerk-treasurer. 
(3)  If a license for game/amusement devices is issued, it shall be applicable to all game/amusement devices permitted upon a particular premises and shall set forth the maximum number of game/amusement devices that may be placed therein. Should a licensee have on his premises a number of game/amusement devices in excess of that permitted by the license, it shall constitute one of the grounds for suspension or revocation of the license and permit under section 3-52. 
(f)  Fees. 
(1)  The fees required under the provision of this section shall be as follows: 
a.  For each application for a premises permit, the sum of $25.00; 
b.  For each application for a game/amusement device license, the sum of $20.00; 
c.  For each premises permit, the sum of $100.00 annually for each such permit; and 
d.  For premises having games/amusement devices, for each game/amusement device authorized by license, the sum of $35.00 annually, the sum thereof representing the total annual license fee. 
(2)  All fees provided for herein shall be nonrefundable and without proration. 
(3)  The board of trustees may, from time to time, amend, repeal, abolish or otherwise modify any fee provided for herein by order or resolution of the board. Except for good cause shown, and unless specifically provided for therein no such order or resolution shall be retroactive, in either its effect or application, from the date of its adoption. 
(g)  The building inspector or such other designee of the village board of trustees shall periodically review and examine each premises for which a premises permit has been issued to assure full compliance with the provisions of this law and will provide a report of all violations discovered to the board promptly. 
(Code 1978, § 4-21; L.L. No. 4-1981, § 2; L.L. No. 5-1982, §§ 1, 2; L.L. No. 4-1988, § 1; L.L. No. 01-2002) 
Sec. 3-50. - Location restrictions relating to the use, operation, etc., of games and amusement devices. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to own, lease, store, possess, use, operate or maintain any game or amusement device for business and for commercial purposes within the village and no license or permit shall be granted or issued therefor, within any of the following restricted locations or premises: 
(1)  Any area of the village which is zoned for a use classification other than general business classification under the zoning laws, ordinances, rules or regulations of the village; 
(2)  Any area within a 500-foot radius of any school, nursery, day care center, church, synagogue, public park or playground, library, hospital or clinic, public building or community center, or nursing home; 
(3)  Any open area, open court or other mandatory open portion on any lot, plot or premises; 
(4)  Any area within a 250-foot radius of any place or premises, other than a bar or bar-restaurant, in which any game or amusement device is currently and lawfully used, stored, owned, leased, possessed, operated or maintained under a valid license or permit issued pursuant to this article; 
(5)  Within or upon any place, premises or building, other than a bar or bar-restaurant, in which any type of food, beverage, liquor or alcoholic beverage is or may be sold, offered for sale, purchased, dispensed, served or consumed, or in which the same is permitted to be brought into or possessed in or upon any part or portion of such place, premises or building; 
(6)  Within or upon any place, premises or building, any part or portion of which is designed, constructed, altered, intended, used or maintained as or for a residential dwelling or apartment, whether or not the same shall be segregated from the remainder of such premises, and whether or not the same shall be located on the same or a different floor of such building or premises as the remaining portion thereof. 
(b)  The provisions of this section shall not apply to any establishment actually licensed by the village for the use, operation or maintenance of any game or amusement device installed and in operation prior to October 1, 1982, solely in respect to any such game or amusement device actually covered under the provisions of any such license for a period of six months from October 1, 1982, unless extended by resolution of the board of trustees. Upon the expiration of the term provided for hereby, or the expiration of the term specified in a resolution adopted by the board of trustees, if any, this section shall apply fully, with equal force and effect to every person, place, premises and building within the village. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to own, lease, store, possess, use, operate or maintain any game or amusement device for business or commercial purposes within the village and no license or permit shall be granted or issued therefor where the intended scope of operations or existing operations: 
(1)  Permit a person under the age of 16 years to be permitted on said premises during the hours when schools are in session, and during the time when the curfew is in effect as provided by section 12-44. 
(2)  When the premises shall be open for operation between the hours of midnight and 9:00 a.m. or any part thereof. 
(3)  When insufficient adult supervisory employees are on premises. 
(Code 1978, § 4-22; L.L. No. 4-1981, § 2; L.L. No. 5-1982, § 3) 
Sec. 3-51. - Area requirements. 
    Every game and amusement device within the village shall be so situated and placed within and upon a premises that it shall not: 
(1)  Block or otherwise obstruct any window, door, doorway, ventilating duct, fire exit, boiler, furnace, radiator, baseboard or other heater device, stairs or stairway, toilet or other sanitary facility; 
(2)  Obstruct, encumber or otherwise interfere with the free, clear passage of any person into, through, or from such premises; or 
(3)  Have an open, unobstructed area, surrounding such game or device, from floor to ceiling, of less than five feet, measured from each of the actual exterior sides of every such game or device, except the one side (and no more than one) which is placed near or against a wall or partition. 
(Code 1978, § 4-23; L.L. No. 4-1981, § 2) 
Sec. 3-52. - Suspension or revocation; appeals. 
(a)  Any license or permit issued pursuant to the provisions of this law may be suspended or revoked by order of the board of trustees or by order of the village clerk-treasurer or building inspector for a violation of any of the provisions of this law. The effective date of any such revocation or suspension shall be the date of service of a written notice of same, and such notice shall be deemed served, in compliance with this section, on the date that same shall be either personally served or delivered to the person to whom the license or permit was issued, or on the date such notice is mailed, return receipt requested, by either certified or registered mail, to the last known address of the holder thereof as the same shall appear on the most recent application for such license or permit. 
(b)  Any person whose license or permit has been suspended or revoked, pursuant to the provisions herein, shall have the right to a hearing before the board of trustees to review such suspension or revocation, provided that such person files a written petition requesting such hearing in the office of the clerk-treasurer within 30 days of the date of service of the notice provided for in subsection (a) of this section. The board of trustees, within 30 days of the date of filing of such petition, shall fix the date for such hearing, and shall hold the same, and render its decision thereon within 60 days of the date of the hearing. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person whose license or permit has been suspended or revoked, or whose license or permit has become null and void after expiration and nonrenewal thereof, to use, operate or maintain any game or amusement device for business or commercial purposes, or to allow any other person to use, operate or maintain the same, within the village, during any period of time after which such license or permit has been suspended, revoked or become null and void, and before which such license and permit has been actually and validly reissued, reinstated or restored. 
(Code 1978, § 4-24; L.L. No. 4-1981, § 2) 
Sec. 3-53. - Off-street parking. 
    In addition to the parking requirements contained in the zoning law of the village as set forth in appendix B, section 12 no license or permit shall be issued or granted for the premises or devices until provision has been made for two parking spaces for each such game or amusement device permitted by this law. Such parking spaces shall be regulated pursuant to the provisions of appendix B, section 12. 
(Code 1978, § 4-25; L.L. No. 4-1981, § 2) 
Sec. 3-54. - Variance of strict applicability of restrictions. 
    Upon consideration of the granting of an application for permit or license, the board of trustees after considering the factors described in section 3-49(d) and upon a proper showing by the applicant that the strict application of the restrictions contained in section 3-50 would cause undue hardship, the board of trustees may vary by waiver or modification of the strict application of the requirements contained in section 3-50. 
(Code 1978, § 4-26; L.L. No. 6-1986, § 1) 
Sec. 3-55. - Waiver of article for existing premises. 
    The village board may, in its sole discretion by resolution, waive the applicability of any provision contained in sections 3-50, 3-51 and 3-53 to a premises which has in use and in operation a game or amusement device on the effective date of L.L. No. 6-1986. 
Secs. 3-56-3-83. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - GAMES OF CHANCE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note- Local Law No. 7-1988, which local law is codified in this article, was approved at a referendum held on November 8, 1988, by a majority of the voters voting thereon. 
State Law reference- Games of Chance Licensing Law, General Municipal Law § 185 et seq. 

Sec. 3-84. - Short title. 
    This article shall be known as the "Games of Chance Law" of the village. 
(Code 1978, § 4-41; L.L. No. 7-1988, § 1) 
Sec. 3-85. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates different meaning: 
    Authorized organization means an authorized organization as defined in General Municipal Law § 186(4.). 
    Games of chance has the same meaning as defined in General Municipal Law § 186(3.). 
(Code 1978, § 4-42; L.L. No. 7-1988, § 2) 
Sec. 3-86. - License; regulations. 
    Authorized organizations may, upon the obtainment of a license from the clerk-treasurer of the village conduct games of chance within the village as provided in General Municipal Law art. 9-A (General Municipal Law § 185 et seq.) and as provided further in this local law. Such games of chance shall be conducted in accordance with the general state law and with the rules and regulations of the state racing and wagering board and this local law. 
(Code 1978, § 4-43; L.L. No. 7-1988, § 3) 
Sec. 3-87. - Signs. 
    No signs advertising the conduct of games of chance within the village shall be permitted except as may be permitted pursuant to the zoning laws of the village and upon complying with the provisions governing same as contained therein. 
(Code 1978, § 4-44; L.L. No. 7-1988, § 4) 
Sec. 3-88. - Conducting games on Sunday. 
    Games of chance on the first day of the week, commonly known as Sunday, may be conducted pursuant to this local law and appropriate statute and regulation. 
(Code 1978, § 4-45; L.L. No. 7-1988, § 5) 
Sec. 3-89. - Control and supervision of games. 
    The chief law enforcement officer of the village shall exercise control over and supervision of all games of chance conducted under an appropriately issued license. Such officer shall have all those powers and duties set forth in General Municipal Law art. 9-A (General Municipal Law § 185 et seq.). 
(Code 1978, § 4-46; L.L. No. 7-1988, § 6) 
Sec. 3-90. - Restrictions on conduct of games. 
(a)  License required. No person other than a licensee under the provisions of General Municipal Law § 191, shall conduct such game or shall lease or otherwise make available for conducting games of chance premises for any consideration whatsoever, direct or indirect. 
(b)  Rental based on receipts. No game of chance shall be held, operated or conducted on or within any leased premises if rental under such lease is to be paid, wholly or partly, on the basis of a percentage of the receipts or net profits derived from the operation of such game. 
(c)  Suppliers.
