The village shall make available the names, addresses, and telephone numbers of those persons who are certified as testers for backflow prevention devices. It shall be the duty of the superintendent to see that certified inspection and operational tests of the backflow prevention devices are made. The customer shall notify the superintendent in advance, in writing, when the tests are to be undertaken so that he or his representative may witness the tests if it is so desired. These devices shall be repaired, overhauled or replaced at the expense of the customer whenever said devices are found to be defective. Copies of all testing and maintenance records shall be sent to the superintendent immediately after the work is performed. 
(f)  All presently installed prevention devices which do not meet the requirements of this section but were approved devices for the purposes described herein at the time of installation and which have been properly maintained, shall, except for the inspection and maintenance requirements under subsection (e) of this section, be excluded from the requirements of these rules so long as the superintendent is assured that they will satisfactorily protect the village's system. Whenever the existing device is moved from the present location or requires more than minimum maintenance or constitutes a hazard to health, the unit shall be replaced by a backflow prevention device meeting the requirements of this section. 
(g)  No water service connection to any customer's water system shall be installed or maintained by the village unless the water supply is protected as required by state laws and regulations and this article. Service of water to any premises shall be discontinued by the village if a backflow prevention device required by this article is not installed, tested and maintained, or if it found that a backflow prevention device has been removed or bypassed. Service will not be restored until such conditions or defects are corrected. 
(Code 1978, § 10-27; L.L. No. 7-1984, § 1) 
Sec. 10-28. - Enforcement and penalties. 
(a)  A violation of the provisions of section 10-27 is a misdemeanor punishable by a fine not to exceed $1,000.00 or by imprisonment not exceeding six months, or by both such fine and imprisonment. In lieu of, or in addition to, such fine and imprisonment or both, each such violation shall be subject to a civil penalty not exceeding $1,000.00 for any one case, to be recovered in an action or proceeding brought by the village attorney in a court of competent jurisdiction. Each day of a continuing violation shall be subject to a separate such fine, imprisonment or civil penalty. 
(b)  The village attorney may maintain an action or proceeding in the name of the village in a court of competent jurisdiction to compel compliance with this article or restrain by injunction any violation of this article, notwithstanding the provisions of subsection (a) of this section for a penalty or other punishment. 
(c)  Where any violation of this article causes expense to the village, such violation may also be punishable by a civil suit against the violator, brought by the village attorney in the name of the village in a court of competent jurisdiction, to recover such additional cost. 
(Code 1978, § 10-28; L.L. No. 7-1984, § 1) 
State Law reference- Penalties for violation of village legislation, Penal Law §§ 55.10, 70.15, 80.05, 80.10, Village Law § 20-2006, Municipal Home Rule Law § 10(4.)(b.). 
Chapter 11 - MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC[1] 
Footnotes:

State Law reference- Obedience to traffic regulations, police officers and flagpersons required, Vehicle and Traffic Law §§ 1101, 1102; applicability of traffic uniformity of traffic regulations, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1600; restrictions upon municipality to regulate traffic, Vehicle and Traffic Law §§ 1600, 1604; municipal regulation of traffic, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1640 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 11-1. - Signs to conform to uniform manual. 
    Signs erected pursuant to this chapter shall be in conformity with the manual of uniform traffic control devices. 
(Code 1978, § 11-1; L.L. No. 2-1975, § 2)

ARTICLE II. - OPERATION OF VEHICLES 

Sec. 11-16. - Speed limits. 
(a)  Maximum speed. Thirty miles per hour is hereby established as the maximum speed at which vehicles may proceed, on or along highways within the corporate limits of this village. 
(b)  Specific streets. The maximum speed at which traffic may proceed along specific streets or portions thereof in the village is hereby established as follows: 
Creek Road extension , between the east village line and the south village line, 40 miles per hour. 
Garden Lane, 15 miles per hour.

State Law reference- Authority to designate one-way streets, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1640(a)4. 
Sec. 11-18. - Bikeways. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Class I bikeway means a travelway exclusively for bicycles. Crossflows by pedestrians and motorists are minimized. It may be either within or outside the right-of-way (property boundaries) of a highway. 
    Class II bikeway means a travelway principally for bicycles. Motor vehicles or pedestrians are not allowed except to reach adjacent driveways or property. Vehicle parking or sidewalks may be adjacent to the bike lane, which itself is separated from adjacent lanes of motorized traffic by striping, cones or a physical barrier. 
    Class III bikeway means a travelway shared with motorized vehicles. It is designated on collector or local streets and has no physical separation from adjacent traffic. (Only streets with low speed limits and traffic volumes should be made class III routes.) 
(b)  Schedule. The following streets or portions thereof are designated bikeways, as indicated: 
Mohawk Street, from North Fifth Street to the east village line, class III. 
North Fifth Street, from Ridge to the north village line, class II. 
(Code 1978, § 11-18; Res. of 10-7-1974)

Sec. 11-21. - Truck route system. 
(a)  A truck route system, upon which all trucks, tractors and tractor-trailer combinations having a total gross weight in excess of five tons are permitted to travel and operate, shall consist of the following highways: 
Center Street, between the east village line and Fourth Street. 
Fourth Street, between Center Street and Oneida Street. 
Oneida Street, between Fourth Street and Second Street. 
Second Street, between Oneida Street and the north village line. 
(b)  All trucks, tractors and tractor-trailer combinations having a total gross weight in excess of five tons are hereby excluded from all highways within this village, except from those highways listed in subsection (a) of this section, except that this exclusion shall not be construed to prevent the delivery or pick up of merchandise or other property along the highway from which such vehicles and combinations are excluded. 
(Code 1978, § 11-21; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 8.00; L.L. No. 1-1988, § 1) 
State Law reference- Truck routes authorized, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1640(a)(20). 
Sec. 11-22. - Riding, driving on sidewalks prohibited. 
    No bicycle, tricycle, automobile or other vehicle propelled or moved by power carried by or upon the vehicle itself shall be allowed upon the sidewalks of the village. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 1, § 30; Code 1978, § 11-22; Code 1978, § 11-22) 
Sec. 11-23. - Prohibited turns. 
(a)  The turning of vehicles by means of a right-hand turn shall be prohibited at the following locations: 
South-bound traffic from North First Street onto Onondaga Street. 
(b)  The turning of vehicles by means of a left-hand turn shall be prohibited at the following locations: 
East-bound traffic from Onondaga Street onto North First Street. 
Traffic exiting from the drive-way onto Center Street at 905 Center Street at Tops Supermarket parking lot. 
(Code 1978, § 11-23; L.L. No. 3-1979, § 4; L.L. No. 8-1989, § 1) 
State Law reference- Authority to regulate or prohibit turns, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1640(a)(2).

ARTICLE III. - STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Stopping, standing and parking generally, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1200 et seq.; authority to regulate or prohibit stopping, standing or parking, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1640(a)(6). 

Sec. 11-35. - Parking-Prohibited at all times. 
    The parking of vehicles in any of the following locations is hereby prohibited: 
Cayuga Street, on the north side, between Fifth Street and Sixth Street, and on the south side, between Eighth Street and Portage Road. 
Cayuga Street, on the north side between a point 105.6 feet east of Seventh Street and its intersection with the east line of Seventh Street. 
Cayuga Street, on the south side between a point 40 feet east of the east line of Seventh Street and its intersection with the east line of Seventh Street. 
Center Street, on the north side from the center line of Smith Street to a point 100 feet east of the center line of Smith Street to a point 33 feet west of the westerly edge of Smith Street; on the south side between Ninth Street and the east village line, and from the east edge of Seventh Street to a point 70 feet east of the center line of the westerly driveway to the 721-735 Center Street Plaza, and between South Eighth Street and Portage Road; and, on the north side, from 9th Street to a point 250 feet westerly from the center line of 9th Street. 
Lewiston Landing Park, in all areas of the park except as specifically permitted as follows: 
(1)  That portion of the part adjacent to and abutting Water Street and Center Street being an area of land 40 feet in depth and 170 feet in length commencing at the center line of Center Street running northerly therefrom. 
(2)  Parking for the handicapped having duly issued parking permits as authorized by Section 1203A of the Vehicle and Traffic Law. 
Niagara Street, on the west side, between Plain Street and Tuscarora Street; on the east side between Center Street and Plain Street. 
Ninth Street, on both sides between a point 50 feet north and a point 50 feet south of the intersection of Center Street. 
North First Street, on the west side, between Oak Street and Onondaga Street.

Onondaga Street, on the north side, between North Third Street and North Fourth Street.

Ridge Street, on the south side, from the east line of North Fourth Street easterly to a point 160 feet from the east side of the Fourth Street sidewalk (as the sidewalk area is so marked upon pavement).

(Code 1978, § 11-35; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 3.00; L.L. No. 6-1968, §§ 13.02, 13.03; L.L. No. 1-1972, § 2; L.L. No. 6-1973, §§ 1, 2; L.L. No. 3-1975, §§ 1, 2; L.L. No. 7-1977, § 1; L.L. No. 3-1978, §§ 1, 4; L.L. No. 3-1979, §§ 1, 2; L.L. No. 10-1983, §§ 2, 3; L.L. No. 2-1984, § 1; L.L. No. 3-1988, § 1; L.L. No. 3-1993, § 1; L.L. No. 1-1997, § A; L.L. No. 2-1998) 
Sec. 11-36. - Same-Emergencies. 
(a)  When traffic conditions in the village, in the judgment of the mayor, acting mayor or chief of police, create or are likely to create hazardous road conditions or road conditions impeding or likely to impede the free movement of fire, health, police, emergency or other vehicular traffic vital to the health, safety and welfare of the community, the mayor, acting mayor or chief of police may declare that an emergency exists in the village, or in a section thereof and prohibit parking in the areas so designated. 
(b)  Upon the declaration of an emergency, appropriate signs shall be posted with the following legend: 
EMERGENCY 
NO PARKING 
POLICE ORDER 
VILLAGE OF LEWISTON 
(c)  No owner or driver of any motor vehicle shall cause, permit or allow any motor vehicle owned or driven by him to be parked or left unattended on any portion of any street in a section of the village designated as an emergency section. 
(Code 1978, § 11-36; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 7.10; L.L. No. 3-1974, § 1) 
Sec. 11-37. - Same-Two hour limit between 9:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m., excluding Sundays and holidays. 
    The parking of vehicles in any of the following locations for a period of longer than two hours between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. is hereby prohibited, except on Sundays and holidays: 
Center Street, between Third Street and Ninth Street, except on the south side from the east edge of Seventh Street to a point 70 feet east of the center line of the westerly driveway to Center Street Plaza. 
(Code 1978, § 11-37; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 4.00; L.L. No. 6-1973, § 3) 
Sec. 11-38. - Same-Prohibited between 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m. during winter months. 
    The parking of vehicles is hereby prohibited on all highways within the village between 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m. from December 1 to April 1. 
(Code 1978, § 11-38; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 5.00) 
Sec. 11-39. - Same-Parallel and angle. 
(a)  Except where angle parking is authorized, every vehicle stopped, standing, or parked wholly upon a two-way roadway shall be so stopped, standing, or parked with the right-hand wheels of such vehicle parallel to and within 12 inches of the right-hand curb or edge of the roadway. 
(b)  Except where angle parking is authorized, every vehicle stopped, standing, or parked wholly upon a one-way roadway shall be so stopped, standing, or parked parallel to the curb or edge of the roadway, in the direction of authorized traffic movement, with its right-hand wheels within 12 inches of the right-hand curb or edge of the roadway, or its left-hand wheels within 12 inches of the left-hand curb or edge of the roadway. 
(c)  Except where angle parking is authorized, every vehicle stopped, standing, or parked partly upon a roadway shall be so stopped, standing, or parked parallel to the curb or edge of the roadway. On a one-way roadway such vehicle shall be facing in the direction of authorized traffic movement; on a two-way roadway such vehicle shall be facing in the direction of authorized traffic movement on that portion of the roadway on which the vehicle rests. 
(d)  Diagonal parking or angle parking is hereby directed and authorized on the following streets and at the following places: 
Cayuga Street, on the north side, between South Ninth Street and Portage Street. 
Ninth Street, on the south side, between Center Street and Cayuga Street. 
North Seventh Street, on the east side, between Center Street and Onondaga Street. 
Water Street, on the west side, from the south end of such street to Onondaga Street. 
(Code 1978, § 11-39; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 6.00; L.L. No. 6-1968, § 13.04) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1203. 
Sec. 11-40. - Penalties. 
(a)  In addition to any authority granted by statute, this section empowers and directs the collection of penalties in the following amounts for illegal standing and parking: 
(1)  A fine of $15.00 for illegal standing and parking if the fine is paid within three business days. 
(2)  A fine of $25.00 for illegal standing and parking if the fine is paid after three business days. 
(3)  A fine of $35.00 for illegal standing and parking if the fine is paid after 20 business days. 
(b)  In addition to any authority granted by statute, this section empowers and directs the collection of penalties in the following amounts for illegal parking or standing in fire lanes as set forth in section 8-24 and parking areas established for the handicapped as provided for in Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1203-c: 
(1)  A fine of $20.00 for illegal parking or standing if the fine is paid within three business days. 
(2)  A fine of $25.00 for illegal parking or standing if the fine is paid after three business days. 
(3)  A fine of $40.00 for illegal parking or standing if the fine is paid after 20 business days. 
(c)  In addition to any authority granted by statute, this section empowers and directs the collection of penalties in the following amount for illegal parking as set forth in section 11-36: 
(1)  A fine of $50.00 for illegal parking if the fine is paid within 72 hours for a first offense and $100.00 for every offense thereafter. 
(2)  A fine of $100.00 for illegal parking if the fine is paid after 72 hours and prior to the issuance of a warrant, summons or other paper for the collection thereof. 
(3)  A fine of $150.00 for illegal parking if the fine is paid after the issuance of a warrant, summons or other paper for the collection thereof. 
(d)  It shall be a violation for any person to stop, stand or park a vehicle in any area designated as a place for handicapped parking unless the vehicle bears a handicap parking permit and such vehicle is being used for the transportation of a handicapped or disabled person per the New York State Vehicle and Traffic Law. 
(1)  A fine of $50.00 for illegal parking or standing if the fine is paid within three business days. 
(2)  A fine of $60.00 for illegal parking or standing if paid after three business days. 
(3)  A fine of $75.00 for illegal parking or standing if paid after 20 business days. 
(Code 1978, § 11-40; L.L. No. 6-1968, § 13.06; L.L. No. 11-1975, § 1; L.L. No. 5-1983, § 2; L.L. No. 2-1986, § 1; L.L. No. 2-1990, § 1; L.L. No. 02-2006, § 11-40; L.L. No. 02-2007) 
Sec. 11-41. - Clerk-treasurer authorized to collect fines. 
    The village clerk-treasurer is hereby authorized to collect and receive all fines imposed for violation of any provisions pertaining to parking. 
(Code 1978, § 11-41; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 9.00(f); L.L. No. 3-1974, § 5) 
Sec. 11-42. - Standing-Prohibited at all times. 
    Standing of vehicles in any of the following locations is hereby prohibited:

Sec. 11-43. - Same-Applicability of penalties and authorizations. 
    Penalties and provisions of section 11-40 and the authorizations contained in section 11-41 shall be applicable to a violation of section 11-42. 
(Code 1978, § 11-43; L.L. No. 1-1983, § 1)

Sec. 11-45. - Same-Attached to vehicles.

Onondaga Street, on the north and south side, between Water Street and First Street. 
Water Street, on the east and west side between Onondaga Street and Cayuga Street, except for an area along the east side of Water Street commencing at a point 40 feet south of its intersection with Onondaga Street southerly 300 feet and on the west side of Water Street commencing at a point 170 feet north of the center line of Center Street, southerly to the center line of Center Street.

Sec. 11-46. - 15-minute parking. 
    The parking in any of the following areas for a period exceeding 15 minutes is prohibited:

Sec. 11-47. - Parking areas and parking lots. 
    No person shall park, stand, store or leave a motor vehicle or motorcycle upon any public or privately-owned premises or property, parking areas or parking lot without the consent and permission of the owner or lessee of such premises. 
    To effectuate the prohibition on such premises as above described, a conspicuous sign or signs shall be posted at the entrance to such parking area or parking lot informing the public as to the permitted conditions of parking on such parking area or parking lot. 
(L.L. No. 01-2011) 
Secs. 11-48-11-72. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - REMOVAL AND STORAGE OF VEHICLES 

Sec. 11-73. - Removal authorized. 
    The removal of vehicles by police officers, or fire-policemen in case of subsection (1) of this section, is authorized in the following instances: 
(1)  When any vehicle is parked or abandoned on any highway within this village during a snowstorm, flood, fire or other public emergency which affects that portion of the public highway upon which said vehicle is parked or abandoned; 
(2)  When any vehicle is found unattended on any highway within this village where said vehicle constitutes an obstruction to traffic; 
(3)  When any vehicle is parked or abandoned on any highway within this village where stopping, standing or parking is prohibited; 
(4)  When any vehicle is abandoned, parked, or standing in any area within this village, as referred to in Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1640-a, where stopping, standing or parking is prohibited where a written request has been received as set forth in said section. 
(Code 1978, § 11-53; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 9.00(a)-(c); L.L. No. 5-1983, § 3) 
Sec. 11-74. - Storage authorized. 
    After removal of any vehicle as provided in this article, the peace officer or fire-policeman may store such vehicle in a suitable place at the expense of the owner. 
(Code 1978, § 11-54; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 9.00(d)) 
Sec. 11-75. - Report to chief of police. 
    The peace officer or fire-policeman shall without delay report the removal and the disposition of any vehicle removed as provided in this article to the chief of police. 
(Code 1978, § 11-55; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 9.00(e)) 
Sec. 11-76. - Notification of owner. 
    It shall be the duty of the chief of police to ascertain to the extent possible the owner of a vehicle removed pursuant to this article or the person having charge of the same, and to notify him of the removal and disposition of such vehicle and of the amount which will be required to redeem same. 
(Code 1978, § 11-56; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 9.00(e)) 
Sec. 11-77. - Redemption by owner; fees and charges. 
    The owner or person in charge of a vehicle which has been removed and stored pursuant to this article may redeem the same upon the payment of reasonable and customary charges for such removal and storage. Such charges for removal shall not exceed $25.00 when such removal takes place between the hours of 6:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m., nor $20.00 between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. together with any charges for storage, such charge not to exceed $2.00 per day, or fraction thereof. 
(Code 1978, § 11-57; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 9.00(d); L.L. No. 13-1975, § 1) 
Sec. 11-78. - Reports required as to receipt of redemption fees and charges. 
    Any person receiving a payment for removal and/or storage of a motor vehicle pursuant to the provisions of this article shall file a report with the village clerk-treasurer not later than ten days succeeding the month in which such sums were received indicating the number and make of vehicles removed and/or stored, the dates when such vehicles were removed and/or stored, dates payments were received, amounts of payments, and names of individuals redeeming the vehicles. 
(Code 1978, § 11-58; Ord. of 5-26-1966, § 9(f); L.L. No. 13-1975, § 2) 
Chapter 12 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 12-1. - Creating a hazard. 
(a)  A person is guilty of creating a hazard when: 
(1)  Having discarded in any place where it might attract children, a container which has a compartment of more than 11/2 cubic feet capacity and a door or lid which locks or fastens automatically when closed and which cannot easily be opened from the inside, such person fails to remove the door, lid, locking or fastening device; or 
(2)  Being the owner or otherwise having possession of property upon which an abandoned well or cesspool is located, such person fails to cover the same with suitable protective construction. 
(b)  Creating a hazard is a class B misdemeanor. 
(Code 1978, § 12-1; Res. of 11-16-1953) 
State Law reference- Similar provisions, Penal Law § 270.10. 
Sec. 12-2. - Clinging to, climbing upon trains or vehicles. 
    No person shall seize, hold, or hang onto or get upon any railroad car, locomotive, or other vehicle for the transportation of passengers or freight while the same shall be in motion, within the limits of the village, nor shall any person within the limits of the village get upon any such car, locomotive or vehicle at any time without permission of the person in charge of such car, locomotive or vehicle. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, § 11; Code 1978, § 12-1) 
Sec. 12-3. - Throwing stones, etc., across streets. 
    No person shall in any street, or upon any public ground, throw stones, snowballs, or other missiles, or play ball, or shoot with, or use a bow and arrow, or slingshot. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, § 13; Code 1978, § 12-3) 
Sec. 12-4. - Carrying of weapons restricted. 
    No person shall carry upon his person any dirk, bowie knife, sword, or spear cane, pistol, revolver or slingshot, jimmy brass knuckles or other dangerous or unlawful weapon. This section shall not prohibit police officers or persons authorized by law from carrying dangerous weapons. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, § 19; Code 1978, § 12-4) 
State Law reference- Firearms and other dangerous weapon, Penal Law § 265.00 et seq. 
Sec. 12-5. - Interfering with, damaging property of another. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere with, deface, damage, injure or remove any public or private property within the village, without the consent of the owner. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, §§ 18, 23-25; Code 1978, § 12-5) 
State Law reference- Criminal mischief and related offenses, Penal Law § 145.00 et seq. 
Sec. 12-6. - Discharge of firearms prohibited. 
    The discharge of firearms within the village is prohibited except by police officers in the discharge of their duties. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, § 30; Code 1978, § 12-6; Ord. of 8-7-1918) 
State Law reference- Firearms and other dangerous weapon, Penal Law § 265.00 et seq. 
Sec. 12-7. - Prohibitions as to trailers, etc. 
(a)  No person shall construct, erect, place or cause to be constructed, erected or placed upon real property in the village, including roads, highways and public places located therein, any trailer, car, vehicle of any description, tent, shed, barrack, construction camp, steamer, boat, barge or any other similar structure intended to be used, or used, temporarily or permanently, for the housing, shelter, feeding or entertainment of any person. This provision shall not be deemed to prohibit the use by tourists of trailers or vehicles for such purposes for a period not exceeding 48 hours at places within the village specifically designated by the village board for such uses. 
(b)  No steamer, boat, barge or other similar structure intended to be used, or used, temporarily or permanently, for the housing, shelter, feeding or entertainment of any person shall be attached to any real property, including streets or other public places, within the limits of the village, except as such use shall be incidental to the transportation of persons or property upon regular or scheduled trips between the village and other places. 
(c)  No owner, lessee or occupant of real property shall lease or permit the use of premises owned, leased or occupied by him for the purposes prohibited by subsection (a) or (b) of this section. 
(Code 1978, § 12-7; Res. of 3-2-1942) 
Secs. 12-8-12-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - NOISE 

Sec. 12-19. - Intent. 
    The board of trustees determines that the creation of unreasonable noise within the village limits of Lewiston is detrimental to the comfort, convenience, safety, health and welfare and to the quality of life of the citizens of the village. Therefore, it intends hereby to prohibit all unreasonable noise from all sources, subject to its police power, in order to preserve, protect and promote the health, safety and welfare and the peace, quiet, comfort and repose of all persons within the village. 
(Code 1978, § 12-19; L.L. No. 2-2001) 
Sec. 12-20. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Person means any individual, business, firm, corporation, association, club, partnership, society or any other form of association or organization. 
    Property being used for nonresidential purposes means the imaginary line, including its vertical extension, that separates one parcel or real property from another, or the vertical and horizontal boundaries of a dwelling unit located within a multiple dwelling unit building. 
    Property being used for residential purposes means property which contains one or more dwelling units, including, but not limited to, single-family attached or detached dwelling units, multiple dwellings, hotels, motels, senior citizen housing, adult residential care facilities, nursing homes, dormitories, sororities and fraternities. 
    Sound reproduction devices means any devices, instrument, mechanism, equipment or apparatus for the amplification of any sounds from any radio, phonograph, tape player, compact disc player, musical instrument, television, loudspeaker, or other sound-making or sound-producing device, or any device or apparatus for the reproduction or amplification of the human voice or other sound used for entertainment purposes. 
    Unreasonable noise means any noise defined in section 12-23. 
(Code 1978, § 12-20; L.L. No. 2-2001) 
Sec. 12-21. - Unreasonable noise prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to make, continue, cause to be made or permit to be made any unreasonable noise within the geographic boundaries of the village , or within those areas over which the village has jurisdiction. 
(Code 1978, § 12-21; L.L. No. 2-2001) 
Sec. 12-22. - Determination of unreasonable noise. 
    A determination as to the existence of unreasonable noise may be established by the specific acts enumerated within section 12-23. 
(Code 1978, § 12-22; L.L. No. 2-2001) 
Sec. 12-23. - Specific acts prohibited. 
    The following acts and the causes thereof are declared to be in violation of this article: 
(1)  The use of any sound reproduction device outside of a structure, whereby the sound emitted from such device is audible on property being used for residential purposes at a point more than 100 feet from the real property boundary line of the property from which said noise emanates, excluding Monday through Thursday from 2:00 p.m. to 10:00 p.m.; Friday and Saturday from 2:00 p.m. to 11:00 p.m.; and on Sunday from 2:00 p.m. to 9:00 p.m. 
(2)  The use or operation of any sound reproduction device inside a structure so as to result in the sound, or any part thereof, emitted from such device to be projected therefrom outside the structure, whereby the sound emitted from such device is audible on property being used for residential purposes at a point more than 100 feet from the real property boundary line of the property from which said noise emanates, excluding Monday through Thursday from 2:00 p.m. to 10:00 p.m.; Friday and Saturday from 2:00 p.m. to 11:00 p.m.; and on Sunday from 2:00 p.m. to 9:00 p.m. 
(3)  The use or operation of any sound reproduction device in a vehicle which would constitute a threat to the safety of pedestrians or vehicle operators. 
(4)  The use or operation of any sound reproduction device within 500 feet of any school, church or courthouse while the same is in session so as to interfere with the function of such facility, provided that conspicuous signs are displayed indicating the location of such facility. 
(5)  The use or operation of any sound reproduction device within 500 feet of any hospital, nursing home or medical facility so as to interfere with the function of such facility or so as to disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of a reasonable person of normal sensitivities while confined to or being treated at such facility, provided that conspicuous signs are displayed indicating the location of such facility. 
(6)  Powered equipment. 
a.  The outdoor use or operation of any powered tool or equipment, including, but not limited to, saws, drills, grinders, lawn mowers or tractors, leaf blowers or any other garden tools or equipment on property being used for residential purposes between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 8:00 a.m. 
b.  The outdoor use or operation of any of the aforementioned tools or equipment between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 8:00 a.m. on property being used for residential purposes and at any time on property being used for nonresidential purposes so as to disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of a reasonable person of normal sensitivities. 
(7)  The use or operation of any audible burglar alarm or motor vehicle burglar alarm, unless such burglar alarm shall be capable of and shall automatically terminate its operation within 15 minutes of being activated. If a burglar alarm, whether residential, business or motor vehicle, activates on two or more occasions within a one-year period, and such activation was not due to an actual attempt at entry into the residence, business or motor vehicle, such that it was a false alarm, then the owner of said alarm is required to have the alarm repaired or calibrated so as to eliminate the false alarm and attendance disturbance. 
(8)  The operation of any motor vehicle with a gross vehicle weight rating in excess of 10,000 pounds, or any auxiliary equipment attached to such motor vehicles, for a period longer than 15 minutes in any hour while the vehicle is stationary, for reasons other than traffic congestion, so that the sound emanated therefrom is audible on property being used for residential purposes between the hours of 9:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. of the following day. This provision shall not apply to authorized emergency vehicles or to public utility vehicles actually engaged in emergency operations. 
(9)  The operation, repair, rebuilding, modifying or testing of any motor vehicle, motorcycle, motorboat, go-cart or minibike on property being used for residential purposes so as to disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of a reasonable person of normal sensitivities. 
(10)  The use or operation of a refuse-collecting vehicle anywhere which, when collecting or compacting, projects sound which is audible on property being used for residential purposes between the hours of 9:00 p.m. and 5:00 a.m. of the following day. 
(11)  The owning, possessing or harboring of any animal or bird which shall make sounds which are audible on property being used for residential purposes for a continued or intermittent duration in excess of 30 minutes, or which shall disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of a reasonable person of normal sensitivities. 
(12)  The conduct of any construction activities, including, but not limited to, the erection, demolition, assembling, altering, installing or equipping of buildings, public or private roadways, roads, premises, parks, utility lines or other property, including related activities such as land clearing, grading, earthmoving, excavating, blasting, filling or landscaping, so as to project a noise therefrom which is audible on a property being used for residential purposes between the hours of 9:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. of the following day. 
(Code 1978, § 12-23; L.L. No. 2-2001) 
Sec. 12-24. - Exceptions. 
    The following sounds shall not be deemed to be in violation of this article: 
(1)  The sound created by bells or chimes associated with a church, synagogue or any other place of public worship. 
(2)  The sound created by any governmental agency or by the use of public warning devices. 
(3)  The sound created by public utilities in carrying out the operation of their function. 
(4)  The sound created by any parade, fair, sporting event, entertainment or other event sponsored by any public organization or private school, provided that such event shall take place between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 11:00 p.m. 
(5)  The sound created by animals in a kennel when the kennel owner has taken all reasonable steps to temper that sound. 
(6)  The sound emanating from any tractors, trucks, combines or any other machinery used for agricultural purposes while planting, harvesting or tending to crops being grown on land zoned for such agricultural purposes. 
(7)  Snow-removal equipment. 
(8)  The sound emanating from a reproduction device situate outside at any public outings, private clubs, restaurants and taverns on Fridays and Saturdays between the hours of 2:00 p.m. and 11:00 p.m.; on Sundays between the hours of 2:00 p.m. and 9:00 p.m.; and Mondays through Thursdays between the hours of 2:00 p.m. and 10:00 p.m., except that in no event shall such sound production violate the provisions of Penal Law § 240.20(2). 
(9)  The sound emanating from a reproduction device situate inside a permanent closed structure at any public outing, private club, restaurant and tavern between 2:00 p.m. and one hour before the last hour authorized by the state liquor authority for the service of alcoholic beverages in licensed facilities except that in no event shall such sound production violate the provisions of Penal Law § 240.20(2). 
(Code 1978, § 12-24; L.L. No. 2-2001) 
Sec. 12-25. - Penalties for offenses. 
    Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a violation and shall be punishable by a fine of not more than $250.00 or imprisonment for not more than 15 days, or both. Each day that such violation occurs shall be deemed a separate offense punishable as such. This article shall be enforced by the Lewiston consolidated police department as well as any other police agency with authority to enforce same. 
(Code 1978, § 12-25; L.L. No. 2-2001) 
State Law reference- Penalties for violation of village legislation, Penal Law §§ 55.10, 70.15, 80.05, 80.10, Village Law § 20-20006, Municipal Home Rule Law § 10(4.)(b.). 
Sec. 12-26. - Authority to grant exception and variances. 
    The board of trustees or its duly authorized representatives shall have the authority to grant special variances, issue temporary permits and suspend any of the provisions of this local law upon such conditions and for such time as it shall deem fit to best serve the public health and welfare and the quality of life in the village. 
(Code 1978, § 12-26; L.L. No. 2-2001) 
Secs. 12-27-12-43. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - CURFEW FOR MINORS 

Sec. 12-44. - Established. 
(a)  No person under the age of 16 years shall be or remain in or upon any of the streets, alleys or public places of the village at night after the hours of 10:00 p.m. during the months from May 1 to November 1 and after the hours of 9:00 p.m. from November 1 to May 1 unless such person is accompanied by a parent, guardian or other person having charge or custody of such minor person or unless such minor person is in the performance of any errand or duty directed by such parent, guardian or other person having charge or custody of such minor person. 
(b)  The hours specified in subsection (a) of this section shall be standard time or daylight saving time, whichever shall be legally in effect. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, § 10; Code 1978, § 12-34; Res. of 8-5-1946) 
Sec. 12-45. - Minors not to engage in vocations requiring presence on streets during prohibited hours. 
    No person under the age of 16 years shall engage in any vocation such as peddling or selling upon the streets, alleys or public places of the village after the hours specified in section 12-44, or in any other vocation which requires the presence of such minor upon the streets, alleys or public places of the village after such hours. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, § 10; Code 1978, § 12-35; Res. of 8-5-1946) 
Sec. 12-46. - Parents, guardians not to permit article violations; exception. 
    No parent, guardian or other person having charge, care and custody of any person under the age of 16 years shall allow or permit any child, ward or other person under such age to go or be in or upon any of the streets, alleys or public places of the village during the time prohibited in this article. 
(Ords. 1904, ch. 3, § 10; Code 1978, § 12-36; Res. of 8-5-1946) 
Sec. 12-47. - Defenses to prosecution. 
    It is a defense to a prosecution under this article that the person under 16 years of age was: 
(1)  On an errand at the direction of the minor's parent or guardian or an adult designated by the minor's parent or guardian, without any detour or stop; 
(2)  In a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel; 
(3)  Engaged in an employment activity, or going to or returning home from an employment activity, without any detour or stop; 
(4)  Involved in an emergency. In this subsection, the term "emergency" means an unforeseen combination of circumstances or the resulting state that calls for immediate action. The term includes, but is not limited to, a fire, a natural disaster, or automobile accident, or any situation requiring immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss of life; 
(5)  Attending an official school, religious, or other recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the village, a civic organization, or another similar entity that takes responsibility for the minor, or going to or returning home from, without any detour or stop, an official school, religious, or other recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the village, a civic organization, or another similar entity that takes responsibility for the minor; 
(6)  Exercising First Amendment rights protected by the United States Constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, and the right of assembly; or 
(7)  Married or had been married or had disabilities of minority removed in accordance with law. 
Secs. 12-48-12-69. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES 

Sec. 12-70. - Possession of alcoholic beverage containers. 
    No person shall drink from, or have in his possession with intent to drink from, any open bottle, can or container, containing liquor, beer, wine or other alcoholic beverage while such person is on any public highway, public street, public parking area, public place or in any vehicle in any public place, excepting those premises duly licensed for the sale and consumption of alcoholic beverages on premises, whatsoever in said village except as hereinafter provided. 
(Code 1978, § 12-40; L.L. No. 5-1980, § 2; L.L. No. 6-1985, § 1) 
Sec. 12-71. - Consumption of alcoholic beverage in public places. 
    No person shall consume liquor, beer, wine or other alcoholic beverage while such person is on any public highway, public street, public parking area, or in any vehicle or public place, excepting those premises duly licensed for sale and consumption of alcoholic beverages on the premises, whatsoever in the village except as hereinafter provided. 
(Code 1978, § 12-41; L.L. No. 5-1980, § 2) 
Sec. 12-72. - Open container as evidence. 
    Any open bottle, can or container, containing or having contained liquor, beer, wine or other alcoholic beverage, found in any vehicle shall be presumptive evidence that the same is in the possession of all the occupants thereof and in violation of this article. 
(Code 1978, § 12-42; L.L. No. 5-1980, § 2) 
Sec. 12-73. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Alcoholic beverage means all alcohol, spirits, liquor, wine, beer, hard cider and every liquid containing alcohol capable of being consumed by a human being. 
    Public place means any and all streets, sidewalks, alleys or other public ways in any and all public parks, squares, spaces, grounds, buildings and parking lots all to which the general public has access. 
(Code 1978, § 12-43; L.L. No. 5-1980, § 2) 
Sec. 12-74. - Exceptions. 
    This article, except for section 12-76, shall not apply to: 
(1)  The village parks designated as Academy Park and Lewiston Landing. 
(2)  Such specific public places as shall be made specifically exempt and for such times and upon such conditions as, by resolution of the board of trustees, they shall determine from time to time. 
(Code 1978, § 12-44; L.L. No. 5-1980, § 2; L.L. No. 5-1988, § 2) 
Sec. 12-75. - Penalty. 
    Any person who violates this article shall be guilty of an offense and shall be subject to a fine not exceeding $250.00. 
(Code 1978, § 12-45; L.L. No. 5-1980, § 2) 
State Law reference- Penalties for violation of village legislation, Penal Law §§ 55.10, 70.15, 80.05, 80.10, Village Law § 20-2006, Municipal Home Rule Law § 10(4.)(b.). 
Sec. 12-76. - Possession of alcoholic beverages. 
    No person under 21 years of age shall possess any alcoholic beverage in a public place, and any alcoholic beverage found to be in the possession of a person under 21 years of age in any such public place shall be confiscated. 
(Code 1978, § 12-46; L.L. No. 5-1988, § 1) 
State Law reference- Alcohol and underage persons, Alcoholic Beverage Control Law § 65 et seq. 
Secs. 12-77-12-99. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - ALARMS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Fire alarm or security alarm installers, General Business Law § 69-l et seq. 

Sec. 12-100. - Title. 
    This article shall be known as the "Village of Lewiston False Alarm Law." 
(Code 1978, § 12-50; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-101. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this article is to protect and promote the health, safety and general welfare of the village by reducing the number of false alarms of fire, intrusion, holdup or other emergencies which contribute to the ineffective use of emergency response agencies, require emergency responses which are susceptible to high accident rates, interfere with genuine emergencies (responses) and produce unnecessary alarm noises to the surrounding community. 
(Code 1978, § 12-51; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-102. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Alarm business means any person engaged in the sale, leasing, installation, maintenance or service of alarm systems or who, in any manner, causes the sale, systems in or on any building, structure or facility within the village. An alarm business shall be licensed through the state. 
    Alarm information notice means a notice or decal posted in a prominent location on a building at which an alarm is operational, which shall contain an assigned identification number. 
    Alarm system means any assembly of equipment or devices arranged to signal the presence of a hazard requiring urgent attention which is directly or indirectly connected to police, fire or emergency medical services and to which police, fire and emergency medical services agencies are expected to respond. An alarm system shall include automatic dialing devices. 
    Alarm user means any person using an alarm, including the owner or lessee of real property where an alarm is located. 
    Automatic dialer means any device that automatically dials and relays a prerecorded message to an emergency agency. 
    False alarm means activation of an alarm system through mechanical failure, malfunction, improper installation, no auxiliary power supply, or the negligence of the owner, user, custodian or lessee of any alarm system or of his employees, requiring an emergency response when, in fact, an emergency does not exist, or the intentional activation of an alarm system when the activator knows an emergency situation does not exist. A false alarm does not include alarms activated by violent conditions of nature or similar causes beyond the control of the user, owner or operator of the alarm system. The activation of an alarm system under any circumstances in which the activator reasonably believes that an emergency situation exists shall not be deemed to be a false alarm. 
(Code 1978, § 12-52; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-103. - Registration of alarms. 
(a)  All alarm system users or their designees may register said alarm system with the chief of police of the village police department, on forms by the village police department. 
(b)  Whenever there occurs any change in the information provided on said registration, the alarm system user or his designee shall provide said changes to the village police department. 
(Code 1978, § 12-53; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-104. - False alarm fees. 
(a)  It is hereby found and determined that false alarms requiring the police and/or fire department to respond constitutes a public safety hazard and nuisance. 
(b)  An owner or lessee of real property to which an emergency agency responds as a result of a false alarm shall pay a fee for each such response in each calendar year as follows: 
(1)  Police department response. 
a.  First false alarm       no charge 
b.  Second false alarm       $25.00 
c.  Third and over false alarm, each        50.00 
(2)  Fire department response. 
a.  First false alarm response       no charge 
b.  Second false alarm response       $ 50.00 
c.  Third and over false alarm, each        100.00 
(c)  For purposes of this section, the term "calendar year" for 2002 shall commence on the effective date of the local law from which this article is derived. 
(d)  Notice of excessive use. The owner or lessee of real property which received an emergency response by reason of a false alarm shall be notified, in writing, by means of first-class mail of all avoidable alarms up to five police alarms and/or one fire alarm in a calendar year. The letter shall inform the owner or lessee of real property of the times and types of emergency responses provided to the address location and shall contain a copy of this article. 
(e)  The failure to pay service fees assessed pursuant to this section within 30 days of written notice from the village clerk-treasurer's office of the imposition of the fee is a violation of this article. 
(f)  Payment of charges. False alarm fees shall be paid to the: 
Village Clerk of the Village of Lewiston 
145 N. Fourth Street 
Lewiston, New York 14092. 
(Code 1978, § 12-54; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-105. - Administrative review. 
    An owner of real property or lessee thereof on which an alarm system has been installed and who has been notified of a false alarm may present evidence as to why any such alarm should not be classified as a false alarm to the village code enforcement officer. The police chief and/or fire chiefs shall designate three members of their departments, not to exceed three in total, to receive such evidence and make recommendations and findings of fact concerning such classification. All burglar alarm calls shall be referred to the police chief and/or his designee for a determination and recommendation to the code enforcement officer. All fire alarm calls shall be referred to the fire bureau or its designee for a determination concerning a classification, which determination shall be reviewable only pursuant to procedures under Civil Practice Law and Rules art. 78 (Civil Practice Law and Rules § 7801 et seq.). To challenge the classification of an alarm as a false alarm, the real property owner or lessee thereof, or the alarm business responsible for maintenance of the alarm, shall, in writing, notify the code enforcement officer at the: 
Village of Lewiston 
145 N. Fourth Street 
Lewiston, New York 14092 
within 20 days after the receipt of notice of a false alarm. The failure to give timely notice shall be deemed a waiver of the right to review the determination. 
(Code 1978, § 12-55; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-106. - Alarm information notice; failure to post. 
(a)  Alarm users shall be subject to a service fee as set forth from time to time by resolution of the village board for each occurrence which the police or fire departments respond to an alarm at a building in which an alarm is operational, but the alarm information notice required by section 12-103 is not posted. This fee shall be in addition to the service fees and charges imposed pursuant to section 12-103. 
(b)  The failure to pay service fees assessed pursuant to this section within 30 days of written notice from the village clerk-treasurer's office of the imposition of the fee shall result in an additional charge as set forth from time to time by resolution of the village board for each occurrence for which a service fee has been assessed. The failure to pay service fees assessed pursuant to this section within 30 days of written notice from the village clerk-treasurer's office of the imposition of the fee is a violation of this article. Service charges shall be paid to the: 
Village Clerk of the Village of Lewiston 
145 N. Fourth Street 
Lewiston, New York 14092. 
(c)  Inspection for displaying of the alarm information notice shall be conducted by the village code enforcement officer during periodic fire inspections. The code enforcement officer shall notify, in writing, by first class mail, any property owner or lessee where an alarm information notice is not properly posted. The property owner or lessee shall properly post the required alarm information notice within 15 days of the receipt of notice. Failure to properly post the alarm information notice within 15 days shall be an occurrence, as defined in subsection (a) of this section. 
(Code 1978, § 12-56; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-107. - Restrictions on alarm systems. 
(a)  No person shall install or maintain an external audible alarm device which does not contain an operational automatic cutoff system which turns off the external audible alarms after a period not to exceed ten minutes after activation. 
(b)  An automatic dialer shall be connected directly to the county sheriff's department or state police dispatcher and shall automatically disconnect and/or terminate its message after the message has been transmitted a maximum of two times. Notwithstanding the foregoing, however, the total transmission time of all messages shall not exceed five minutes. 
(Code 1978, § 12-57; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-108. - Connection to emergency agencies. 
(a)  No alarm system shall have an automatic dialer feature or other type of alarm alert which connects automatically to enhanced 911 or the 911 emergency telephone system. 
(b)  There shall be no automatic alarm systems with direct communication of any type to an emergency agency without prior written authorization from the emergency agency where the alarms terminate. 
(Code 1978, § 12-58; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-109. - Enforcement. 
    The village police department and code enforcement officer or designee shall enforce this article. For that purpose, the police department and the code enforcement officer and designee are authorized to issue and serve appearance tickets. The building inspector for the village shall be the code enforcement officer for purposes of this section. 
(Code 1978, § 12-59; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-110. - Limitation of ability. 
    Nothing in this article shall be construed or interpreted to place the village or any of its officers or agents under any obligation or duty to an alarm user or to any person hereunder by reason of this article. The village specifically disclaims any and all liability for any and all damages which may be in any way related to the failure or inability to respond to any alarm. 
(Code 1978, § 12-60; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-111. - Compliance. 
    The owners and lessees of premises having alarm systems shall comply with sections 12-107 and 12-108 on or before January 31, 2003. 
(Code 1978, § 12-61; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Sec. 12-112. - Penalties for offenses. 
    Any person or other entity that does not pay the fees as established in this article shall be subject to a civil penalty in an amount not less than twice the amount of such unpaid fees, but not to exceed $1,000.00 for each offense. Any person or other entity that violates any other provisions of this article shall be subject to a civil penalty in an amount not less than twice the amount of such unpaid fees, but not to exceed $1,000.00 for each offense. A separate offense shall be deemed committed upon each day during which a violation occurs, continues or is permitted. 
(Code 1978, § 12-62; L.L. No. 03-2002) 
Secs. 12-113-12-134. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - SEX OFFENDER REGISTRATION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Sex offender registration, Corrections Law § 168 et seq. 

Sec. 12-135. - Legislative intent. 
    The village recognizes that the county legislature by resolution of March 21, 2006, has urged municipalities throughout the county to adopt legislation concerning the registration of sex offenders in order to protect the citizen of each municipality. The village board believes it to be the utmost concern and priority to protect its citizens from certain types of sex offenders who have been deemed by their risk assessment level to pose a significant risk for re-offending. The village acknowledges the existence of Correction Law art. 6-C (Corrections Law § 168 et seq.) o referred to as the "Sex Offender Registration Act" but believes that this article is allowed by the Municipal Home Rule Law and is necessary in furtherance of the safety of the community. 
(Code 1978, § 12-65; L.L. 03-2006, § 1) 
Sec. 12-136. - Definitions. 
    The definitions as contained in Correction Law § 168-a are adopted as the definitions of this article. 
(Code 1978, § 12-66; L.L. 03-2006, § 2) 
Sec. 12-137. - Registration content. 
    Such registration with the village police department shall include, at a minimum, the following information: 
(1)  Legal name of the level II or level III sex offender (registrant), including any nicknames or aliases, which may have been used or applied for. 
(2)  Date of birth. 
(3)  Social security number. 
(4)  Current address and proposed address where such person has resided or intends to reside within the village. Additionally, any residences owned, purchased, leased, rented or to which such registrant may in any way be entitled in law or equity. 
(5)  Any address where such registrant stays or intends to stay within the village. 
(6)  The current and/or prospective place of employment as well as the address and telephone number and immediate supervisor of such registrant. Additionally, the hours which such registrant is assigned to work. 
(7)  Drivers' license identification number, as well as the vehicle identification number and license plate number of any vehicle owned, leased, utilized or otherwise driven by such registrant either during the course of employment or otherwise. 
(Code 1978, § 12-67; L.L. 03-2006, §§ 3, 4) 
Sec. 12-138. - Additional registration requirements. 
(a)  Should the registrant intend or desire to change his place of residence or employment, such change must be reported to the village police department before the same occurs. The information previously required of the registrant shall similarly be required for any prospective change. 
(b)  In the discretion of the village police department, any level II or level III sex offender who is registering pursuant to this local law shall submit to fingerprinting, photographing of his person, a DNA sample, dental imprints, a description of other indemnifying features or marks, shoe size and any other identifying information that the village police department deems necessary. 
(c)  Such registration shall occur at least annually thereafter for a period of 20 years. Any sex offender who is convicted of two or more separate level II or level III sex offenses must register for life. 
(d)  In the event of any change in registration information, or the addition of new or different information from the item of the initial or subsequent registration, such change shall be provided within three days of the time such new information is available to or otherwise know or within ability of the registrant to know. 
(Code 1978, § 12-68; L.L. 03-2006, § 5) 
Sec. 12-139. - Local registry. 
(a)  The village police department shall maintain a local registry of the particular sex offenders required to register under this article separate and distinct from the registry maintained pursuant to the Corrections Law. It shall specifically state that the registration is required under the Corrections Law. The village police department and/or the village may make available and disseminate such registration information as authorized by state law. 
(b)  In the event that any conviction of a level II or level III sex offender is reversed or set aside by appellant process or order of any court of competent jurisdiction, such data and/or order of the court shall be supplied by the sex offender to the village police department by way of certified copy and the village shall then strike from such registry such reversed or set-aside conviction. 
(c)  The village and the police department make no determination regarding the probability of recidivism the current propensity for criminal activity for any registrant purpose. The purpose of such data in registry is so that information is generally available and accessible rather than to constitute a specific warning about any specific registrant. 
(Code 1978, § 12-69; L.L. 03-2006, § 6) 
Sec. 12-140. - Residency and restrictions. 
    Level II and level III sex offenders shall not reside permanently or temporarily, or acquire any real property by purchase, lease, land contract, rental agreement of or tenancy or otherwise, or establish any place of lodging within a radius of 1,000 feet of all schools, playgrounds, parks, daycare centers, nursing homes, assisted living facilities or fire hall. 
(Code 1978, § 12-70; L.L. 03-2006, § 7) 
Sec. 12-141. - Village contracts. 
    All entities or persons entering into agreements with the village shall conduct background checks of all of its agents, servants or employees to determine whether or not such person may be a level II or level III sex offender as defined in the Corrections Law. Immediate notification shall be provided to the village of any such person. The proposed contractor shall then verify that such person shall not perform work within any of the afforested restricted areas unless specifically supervised by a designated superior of such entity or person. Failure by any contractor to comply with this provision shall be deemed to be a material breach of the contract, allowing the village to negate such contract without penalty. 
(Code 1978, § 12-71; L.L. 03-2006, § 8) 
Sec. 12-142. - Indemnification of village. 
    This article will not be deemed to create or have created any cause of action against the village, which may not be authorized under any other existing law. The village is not liable to any person who may hereafter be harmed who claims or may claim that notice under this article may have or would have prevented such harm. 
(Code 1978, § 12-72; L.L. 03-2006, § 9) 
Sec. 12-143. - Penalties for offenses. 
    Any violation of this article including the providing of inaccurate information is hereby deemed to be an offense separate and distinct from any violation of the Corrections Law. Violations of this article shall be punishable by maximum of 15 days in the county jail or a fine of $250.00 or both. Every day in which a level II or level III sex offender fails to register or is in any way in violation of this article shall be considered and constitute a separate offense. For purposes of any separate criminal prosecution or Corrections Law prosecution, jeopardy shall not be deemed to have attached by a way of violation of this local law should a conviction occur hereunder. Similarly, a conviction of any violation of the Corrections Law of criminal law shall not be deemed to exonerate such convicted party from prosecution under this article. It is the specific intent of the village that any violation of this article is a separate and distinct offense from any violation of the New York State Corrections Law or Penal Law. 
(Code 1978, § 12-72; L.L. 03-2006, § 10) 
State Law reference- Penalties for violation of village legislation, Penal Law §§ 55.10, 70.15, 80.05, 80.10, Village Law § 20-2006, Municipal Home Rule Law § 10(4.)(b.). 
Chapter 13 - PARKS AND RECREATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to dedicate property as playground or recreation center, General Municipal Law § 241. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 13-1. - Park defined. 
    The term "park" shall mean places so designated by resolution of the board of trustees from time to time and located within the village; places owned or leased by the village and operated by the village for parks and recreation purposes. Parks shall be deemed public places so as to make applicable to such parks and recreation areas those portions of the Code applicable to public places. 
(Code 1978, § 13-1; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 1) 
Sec. 13-2. - Management of parks. 
(a)  The supervision, use and management of all public parks within the village shall be under the director of public works, subject to the direction of the board of trustees of the village and subject to the provisions of this article. 
(b)  Whenever a permit is authorized to be issued as provided by sections 13-4 and 13-5, every person claiming to have such permit or permission shall produce and exhibit the same upon the request of any authorized person. All permits shall be subject to the provisions of this article, and the holders thereof must strictly observe the conditions thereof and the provisions of the laws of the village relating to the same. Any permit may be peremptorily revoked by the board of trustees, director of public works or chief of police in case of any violation of the terms on which the same was issued or of any law relating to the same by the holder thereof. 
(c)  No person shall refuse to obey any orders or requests of the director of public works or any policeman having for their objects, the preservation of the parks within the village, their contents or maintenance of order or decorum therein. 
(Code 1978, § 13-2; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 7) 
Sec. 13-3. - Penalties. 
    Any person violating any provision of this article shall be guilty of an offense and shall be fined not more than $250.00 for each offense, and in addition thereto, shall be subject to a civil action for any damages sustained by the village because of such violation. 
(Code 1978, § 13-3; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 8) 
State Law reference- Penalties for violation of village legislation, Penal Law §§ 55.10, 70.15, 80.05, 80.10, Village Law § 20-2006, Municipal Home Rule Law § 10(4.)(b.). 
Sec. 13-4. - Permits required for certain activities. 
    A permit shall be obtained from the board of trustees by persons conducting, operating, presenting or managing any of the following activities: 
(1)  Picnics, outings or gatherings sponsored by an organization or individuals numbering 25 or more persons. 
(2)  Contests, exhibits, dramatic performances, spectacles, plays, motion pictures, radio or television broadcasts, fairs, circuses, shows, musical events or any similar events. 
(3)  The sale of articles or things as a regularly licensed concessionaire. 
(4)  Announcing, advertising or calling to the public's attention articles or services for hire. 
(5)  The reservation of any park facilities for a certain person or group of persons to the exclusion of others. 
(6)  All activities requiring written permission of the board of trustees as hereinbefore specified. 
(Code 1978, § 13-4; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 8A) 
Sec. 13-5. - Standards for issuance of permits. 
    The board of trustees may issue a permit when it finds that: 
(1)  The proposed activity or use of the park will not unreasonably interfere with or detract from the general public enjoyment of the park or cause annoyance or the disturbance of any other person's reasonable use of park facilities, or cause annoyance or disturb the peace of persons residing near the park, or interfere with the maintenance of the park or its facilities. 
(2)  The proposed activity and use will not unreasonably interfere with or detract from the promotion of the public health, welfare, safety and recreation. 
(3)  The proposed activity and use is not unreasonably anticipated to cause violence, crime or disorderly conduct. 
(4)  The proposed activity will not entail unusual, extraordinary or burdensome expense or police supervision by the village. 
(5)  The facilities desired have not been reserved for another use at the date and hour required in the application. 
(Code 1978, § 13-5; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 9) 
Sec. 13-6. - Prohibited activities-Generally. 
    No person shall permit any activity to occur in the village park which is prohibited by chapter 5, chapter 9, chapter 11, chapter 12, chapter 14, section 17-42 and chapter 19. 
(Code 1978, § 13-6; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 2) 
Sec. 13-7. - Same-Specific regulations. 
(a)  Advertising. No person shall post, paint, affix, distribute, deliver or leave any place within a park any placards, tickets, handbills, circulars or advertisements of any kind or nature for advertising purposes, or operate any advertising devices for the purpose of attracting attention to any exhibition, show, performance or display or purpose or solicit passengers for hire. 
(b)  Dangerous behavior. No person shall throw stones or other missiles; annoy others; interfere with, encumber, obstruct or render dangerous any task, driveway, walk or public place in such park, or climb upon any wall, fence, shelter, seat, structure or other improvement in the park, or enter or leave any park except at established entranceways or exists; introduce, carry or discharge any firearms, fireworks or other explosives within a park or throw or deposit on any walk, path, floor or platform any litter or refuse of any kind. 
(c)  Fires. No person shall kindle or maintain any fire within a park, excepting in places provided for that purpose. When any fire is maintained in such place so designated, by any person, then the fire shall be under the care and direction of a competent person from the time it is kindled until it is extinguished. 
(d)  Hours of operation. No person shall, between the hours of sunset and 9:00 p.m. remain at any place in any park in the village where there is no artificial light, nor between 9:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. under any circumstances within any park in the village. 
(e)  Camping prohibited. No person shall lodge or camp in any park in the village, excepting at places designated by the board of trustees. 
(f)  Sleeping on benches prohibited. No person shall sleep upon, lie upon or overturn any seat or bench in any park in the village. 
(g)  Glass beverage containers-Prohibited. No person shall have in his possession any open glass beverage container while such person is in any public park or on any public highway, public street, public parking area or in any vehicle or public place adjacent to any public park. 
(h)  Same-Presumptive evidence. Any open glass beverage container found in any vehicle while in any public park or on any public highway, public street, public parking area or in any public place adjacent to any public park shall be presumptive evidence that the same is in the possession of all the occupants thereof and in violation of subsection (g) of this section. 
(i)  Same-Beverage defined. For the purposes of subsections (g) and (h) of this section, the term "beverage" is defined as every liquid capable of being consumed by a human being. This would not include baby formula in a glass bottle. 
(Code 1978, § 13-7; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 3) 
Sec. 13-8. - Recreational regulations. 
(a)  Wading or swimming. No person shall wade or swim in any park waters or waters adjacent to any park in the village, except at such time and in such places as may be specifically designated with appropriate signs by the director of public works. 
(b)  Use of boats, etc. No person shall launch or recover any boat, canoe or raft from any park lands of the village, except at such time and in such places as may be specifically designated with appropriate signs by the director of public works. 
(c)  Coasting. No person shall coast with vehicles or sleds on wheels or runners at any place within any park within the village except at such places and at such times as may be designated therefor by the director of public works. 
(d)  Games; picnics. No person shall throw, kick or strike any ball or object or pass the same or any other object or play or engage in any games within any park in the village excepting at places designated therefor. Picnics may be had in such parks of the village as shall be designated therefor by the director of public works, and portions of parks may be set off for games, subject to such regulations as may be prescribed by the board of trustees. 
(e)  Construction of platforms, etc.; meetings, ceremonies, etc. No person shall, without the written permission of the board of trustees, erect any structure, stand or platform within any park of the village, for the purposes mentioned in this section, and no person shall hold any meeting, perform any ceremony, make any speech or address, exhibit to the public any performance in whole or in part or engage in any parade or other procession or run any race, without the written consent of the board of trustees. 
(f)  Skating. No person shall use skates of any kind within any village park excepting at such times and at such places as may be designated therefor by the director of public works; nor shall any person skate, slide, walk or go upon any ice, excepting at such times and at such places as may be designated therefor by the director of public works. 
(Code 1978, § 13-8; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 4) 
Sec. 13-9. - Property injury or damage. 
(a)  No person shall injure, write upon, deface, displace, remove, destroy or tamper with any drive, path, walk, bridge or approach thereto, or disturb or remove any asphalt, concrete, flagstone, rock, gravel, sand or earth or make any excavation of any kind, or injure or remove any ice, or injure, displace or remove any structure, building, post, bench, seat, telephone, telegraph, pipe, receiving basin, covers, manholes or vents or any appurtenances or appendages connected therewith, or any other property or equipment, real or personal, owned by the village or under the jurisdiction or control of the village appertaining to the use, management or maintenance of any park in the village, or injure or in any way interfere with any machine, instruments or contrivance used in the parks, or deface, remove or injure any signs, inscription, post or monument within any such park, or any lamps, lights, or apparatus connected therewith and used in any parks, without the written permission or direction of the director of public works. 
(b)  No person shall destroy, cut, injure or remove any plant, flower, shrub, tree or growing thing, or pile any material or debris against the same, or attach any rope, cable or any other contrivance thereto, or enter or walk upon planted place within any park of the village. 
(Code 1978, § 13-9; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 5) 
State Law reference- Criminal mischief and related offenses, Penal Law § 145.00 et seq. 
Sec. 13-10. - Vehicle regulations. 
(a)  No person shall drive any vehicle upon any walk, path or part of any park in the village not designated for vehicle use; no person shall ride any bicycle or similar vehicle on any walk or footpath within any park in the village; no person shall park or permit to be parked any vehicle within any park outside of designated parking places. 
(b)  Whenever any police officer shall indicate or direct by gesture or otherwise, the speed or force of any vehicle within a park in the village, the driver thereof shall immediately obey such direction. 
(Code 1978, § 13-10; L.L. No. 3-1980, § 6) 
Sec. 13-11. - Speed on waterways. 
(a)  Watercraft defined. The term "watercraft" means all manner of devices, gasoline-powered or otherwise, submersible and/or floating and as also defined in the Navigation Law of the state. 
(b)  Speed limit established. There is hereby established a speed limit for watercraft on the waters of the Niagara River between the northerly line of Onondaga Street as extended into the river and the southerly line of Cayuga Street as extended into the Niagara River and for a distance of 100 feet from the shoreline. No watercraft in said area shall exceed five miles per hour and in any event shall not travel at a speed which creates a wake. 
(c)  Violations. A violation of this section shall be punishable by a fine of $25.00 for the first offense, $50.00 for the second offense committed within 24 months and $500.00 for the third or any subsequent offense committed within 24 months. Calculations of time periods for determining successive violation periods shall be those violations occurring within an 18-month period. 
(d)  Enforcement. All police and peace officers and those officers as empowered by federal and state law shall be the enforcement officers of this provision. 
(Code 1978, § 13-11; L.L. No. 2-1989, § 1) 
State Law reference- Penalties for violation of village legislation, Penal Law §§ 55.10, 70.15, 80.05, 80.10, Village Law § 20-2006, Municipal Home Rule Law § 10(4.)(b.). 
Secs. 13-12-13-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PARKS, RECREATION AND CONSERVATION BOARD 

Sec. 13-36. - Created. 
    The village board of trustees hereby creates a board which shall be known as the Village of Lewiston Parks, Recreation and Conservation Board. 
(Code 1978, § 13-16; L.L. No. 1-1980, § 1) 
Sec. 13-37. - Membership. 
(a)  The board created under this article shall consist of seven members who are residents of the village, and shall include by qualifications of interest at least one person in each of the fields of parks, recreation and conservation, who shall be appointed by the mayor, subject to the approval of the board of trustees, and who shall serve at the pleasure of the mayor. 
(b)  Successors to the members of the board shall be appointed to hold office for a term of two years and vacancies shall be filled in the same manner as the original appointment. Vacancies in such board occurring other than by expiration of term shall be filled only for the unexpired term. The mayor is authorized to appoint up to two members to the board who are between the ages of 16 and 21 years. 
(Code 1978, § 13-17; L.L. No. 1-1980, § 1; L.L. No. 3-1983, § 1; L.L. No. 4-1989, § 1) 
Sec. 13-38. - Officers. 
    The mayor, subject to the approval of the village board of trustees, shall designate a member of the board created by this article to act as chairman thereof. At the first meeting of the board, the members thereof shall elect from among themselves a recording secretary. 
(Code 1978, § 13-18; L.L. No. 1-1980, § 1) 
Sec. 13-39. - Meetings. 
    The board created by this article shall adopt rules and procedures for its meetings. It shall keep accurate records of the meetings and activities and shall file an annual report with the board of trustees. 
(Code 1978, § 13-19; L.L. No. 1-1980, § 1) 
Sec. 13-40. - Powers and duties. 
    The powers and duties of the board created by this article shall be to: 
(1)  Be responsible for the formulation and development of policies which govern the regulation and use of all village parks, recreation and conservation programs and related facilities and submitting same for approval by the board of trustees. 
(2)  Ascertain and evaluate recreation and conservation needs and recommend from time to time the establishment, operation and expansion or retrenchment of parks, recreation services and conservation programs with respect to these needs.
